First Day of National Assembly Representatives' Registration: Ding Xuanxiao First to Sign and Be Filmed 28

National Assembly representatives began registering on the 18th. Since the State Council approved this congress as the first session (the previous congress was the Constituent National Assembly), the importance of this congress is evident. Although constitutional governance began on December 25th last year, it has been three months now, but the gathering of the constitutional National Assembly is truly the first time.

The National Assembly registration office is located to the right of the National Fire Assembly Hall, which is a newly built building. The offices of several congress groups are squeezed into a row of small rooms, but a large hall is reserved as a lounge. Before the congress opens, this lounge is the registration office. The registration office is well-organized, with signs posted on the walls and pillars indicating where to sign, where to fill out forms, where to collect travel expenses and documents, and where to rest.

If you are a National Assembly representative, when you walk into the registration office, you will be greeted by the signing area. You must present your certificate of election, then leave your name in the signature book, and collect the registration form and accommodation slip. When filling out the accommodation slip, don't forget to indicate where you plan to stay—whether it is your own residence or a guest house or contracted hotel. After filling out the documents and attaching four 2.5-inch headshots, submit them at the counter opposite and collect a copper token, like a token for withdrawing money from a bank. Oh, this should be added: if you don't have photos or forget to bring them? The preparatory committee has prepared them for you, and you can take photos on the spot, using the photography studio's certificate to replace the photos and sending it to the submission area. Then, you can go to the innermost part of the registration office, which is the lounge, and help yourself to some refreshments. When the issuing office announces the number according to the copper token, you can go there to retrieve a document bag. The document bag includes the following miscellaneous items:

(1) A representative badge, (2) a representative handbook, (3) a directory of registered representatives in Beijing, (4) a receipt for the certificate of election, (5) two postcards for representatives to change their communication address in Beijing, (6) a representative accommodation certificate or hotel introduction slip, (7) a representative payment voucher, (8) a copy of the congress traffic management rules, (9) a copy of the congress shuttle bus rules, (10) a congress representative vehicle survey form, (11) a commission for the congress return or travel to various places during the congress to purchase ticket notification form.

With the "Representative Payment Voucher," you can walk back and receive payment at the payment office. Simply sign and stamp the printed receipt, and you will receive 3.6 million yuan for meals and 4.5 million yuan for accommodation (5 million yuan for official expenses will be issued one week after the opening of the congress). If you want to contact transportation, the staff at the transportation liaison office are waiting for you; if you have matters to commission or inquire about, the inquiry office or service office is also waiting for you. In this way, the registration procedures are completed. If it is not crowded, it only takes four minutes from beginning to end.

Just as more than ninety staff members were quietly waiting for the representatives, the first representative came to register, it was Ding Baoxiao, the regional representative from Jurong County, Jiangsu Province. The Central News Agency photographer and some photojournalists, who had been preparing for a long time, wanted to capture the signing of the first person to register, so Representative Ding became the object of "opening the curtain". In order to make a movie, he was "directed" to pose, and the verification, signing, form collection, form filling, document submission, document retrieval, and payment collection were all filmed, inevitably delaying him a bit. At this time, the second representative to register also arrived. This was Jin Zhen, who came from the artillery, the former mayor of Shenyang, and now participating in the National Assembly as a national border ethnic Manchu representative. No one filmed him, so his procedures were completed quickly, he received the document bag, and obtained the number one badge. When Representative Ding finished filming with a smiling face, he realized that the number one badge had been taken by Mr. Jin. This inevitably caused a small negotiation, he was the first person to register and should receive the number one badge, but the artillery lieutenant general (Jin Zhen) said well: "You have already been on camera, so leave the number one badge to me."

The representatives came sporadically, and the number was not large. The congress staff had nothing to do, and some staff members were using refreshments in the lounge. The refreshments were catered by the Peacock Restaurant of the Central Hotel, and the representatives could take them at will without paying.

Several representatives came without their certificates of election. After inquiring, they could not register, so they had to leave and wait to receive their certificates of election before coming again. In one morning, only seven representatives registered, and the staff exclaimed: "Business is slow." The registration time is from 8:30 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM. More people registered in the afternoon, but the total number for the day was only seventeen. It is said that this is because many people did not know that registration started today, and many people have not yet received their certificates of election. It is estimated that there will be more than 2,700 representatives attending this meeting, and most of them will register at the same time in the few days before the opening, which will be a tense and chaotic scene in the future.

Sun Ke, Mo Dexian, Xu Chuanlin, Liu Dongyan, and Secretary-General Hong Lanyou, who are responsible for preparing for the congress, visited the registration office at 9:30 AM. Besides Hong Lanyou, there was exactly one person each from the Kuomintang, the Democratic Socialist Party, the Youth Party, and social elites. Photojournalists rushed to take photos of them. Sun Ke and others went around the venue, looked at the various arrangements and the staff's work, and nodded repeatedly, expressing their satisfaction.

The work of representative registration has begun. This work will continue until the opening of the congress, and many people are asking: "When will Chairman Chiang come to register?" (Sent from Nanjing on March 18th)

Page 2

Editorial

After President Truman's Two Speeches 29

US President Truman's speech to a joint session of both houses of Congress the day before yesterday is undoubtedly the most important historical document since the end of World War II. From now on, we will have to see how the American people and all countries that love democracy and peace react to President Truman's speech.

In the past half month, the situation in Europe has taken a sharp turn for the worse, almost reaching the final stage of the "Cold War," causing US President Truman, standing on the other side of the Atlantic, to begin to show that his confidence in world peace was wavering. However, the United States after World War II bears a special responsibility in terms of morality and history for maintaining world peace, and its words and actions are related to the safety of the world. Therefore, the people of the whole world, especially those who are threatened by the communist forces, are looking forward to the movements in Washington. At the same time, President Truman himself is deeply aware of the current global crisis and the great responsibility of the United States, and is eager to awaken the vigilance of the American government and the public. Therefore, a few days ago, he decided to deliver a speech to a joint session of both houses of Congress, clarifying the world situation and requesting Congress to take necessary steps to save the situation before it is too late. This diplomatic speech is not only valued by the American government and the public, but also by the people of all countries in the world; in the moment before President Truman delivered his speech, the people of the whole world were probably holding their breath and listening to President Truman's roar.

Now, we have finally heard President Truman's speech on the radio, and at the same time read the full text of this important speech in the telegram. The main points of the speech are summarized as follows: (1) The survival of democracy has been threatened, and it is time for the free men and women of the world to bravely confront the threats to their freedom. (2) The United States must maintain its strong strength to support European countries that are still free and feel threatened by communism and the rule of police states. (3) We must be prepared to pay the price of peace, otherwise we will inevitably pay the price of war. (4) He called for the temporary restoration of the draft and the implementation of universal military training to cope with the serious situation caused by the continuous aggression of the Soviet Union. (5) He requested that Congress act quickly on the $5.3 billion European recovery plan. (6) Our ability to quickly assemble and train a large number of well-trained troops in times of crisis can prevent future conflicts from occurring, and other national policies can restore world stability. (7) Implementing universal military training is enough to declare to the world that we are a support for peace, not only with great determination, but also with the power to achieve peace. (8) We should, regardless of party affiliation, organize a united front and unite with all countries in the world to make every possible effort to maintain world peace.

President Truman's speech was drafted by the President himself in consultation with political, diplomatic, military, and economic experts, and every sentence has a purpose and every word has weight, but because the speech time was only twenty minutes, it could not be explained in detail. However, after President Truman attended the joint session of Congress, he immediately flew to New York to attend the St. Peter's Dinner and gave a speech, more frankly criticizing the Soviet Union's attempt to establish authoritarian rule in the still free countries of Western Europe, and pointed out that communism denies God and does not recognize the right of mankind to self-government, and is in fact a tyranny. He also said that the existence of democracy is currently threatened by communism, and the United States has become the only protector of the free world. At this time, we should unite our strength with the strength of other free people to fight against communism. Therefore, we should use military, economic, and moral strength to support these countries. Although the contents of the two speeches are different, in our opinion, the latter is more powerful and more frank than the former. However, if President Truman only roars and condemns the Soviet Union's aggression and criticizes the communist threat to freedom verbally, and the United States still cannot immediately take effective actions in all aspects to stop the flood of communist forces, then we cannot be sure whether the world's chaos can be immediately reversed.

Looking at Europe in the past half month, the situation is crystallizing. On the one hand, there was first the coup in Czechoslovakia. After the Czech communists seized power, the tragedy of democracy has been repeated. Later, the Soviet Union forced Finland to conclude a mutual assistance treaty. Although it is still in the negotiation stage, Finland, forced by the general trend, is afraid that it will only obey orders. Recently, Europe has been filled with alarming rumors, either that the Soviet Union will take action against Turkey, or that the Soviet Union will require the Nordic countries of Norway and Sweden to sign alliances. The upcoming general election in Italy and the activities of the Communist Party are even more shocking. On the other hand, diplomatic activities are also quite lively. The London Conference decided to merge the three occupied areas of West Germany, and the Bejing Five-Nation Conference has also completed the drafting of the Western European Five-Nation Alliance Treaty, which was signed and established in Paris yesterday, and there is a possibility of expansion. In addition, the European Sixteen-Nation Conference is also being held in Paris. Regardless of the attitude of the representatives of various countries or the course of the meeting, it is enough to show that the countries of Western Europe are united in good faith, unanimously dealing with the threat of communism. Although the United States did not directly participate, the United States is in fact the "guardian" of democratic and free countries, which is an undeniable fact. After reading President Truman's speech, we can especially believe that the US aid policy to Europe will gradually evolve from economic aid to military aid. From this point of view, in addition to the unity of Western European countries themselves, coupled with the full support of the United States, it is logically hoped that the European situation will gradually become clear. However, why hasn't President Truman's speech stabilized the hearts of the world? We believe there are at least two reasons;

First, today's bipolarization of Europe is even more serious than the situation after the Munich Conference in 1938. The aggressor in the past was Nazi Germany. Although Hitler owned Austria and part of Czechoslovakia at that time, the nine countries in Eastern Europe had allied relations with Britain and France. In addition, France was the most powerful country in Europe at that time, and further east, there was a third force - the Soviet Union - restraining it. Looking back at today's Europe, because totalitarian communist countries are always taking the lead, and democratic countries are lagging behind in everything, these two major groups have almost reached a point where their strengths are evenly matched and cannot be compared, both in terms of population and area. Moreover, from the point of view of geographical location or military strategy, the Eastern European group has an advantage, which seems to be beyond the reach of the Western European group. Therefore, the establishment of the Western European Alliance is important today. The five countries of Western Europe not only need to help each other to stop the Soviet Union's military aggression, but also need to work together to prevent the activities of the fifth column within the country. However, according to official observations, its role may not be as great as the world imagines, and looking forward to its future, it is full of thorns, and it is unlikely to be smooth sailing, so we cannot be too optimistic.

Second, although President Truman has frankly expressed his anti-communist stance and frankly announced his support for democratic and free countries, his focus is still on Europe. In particular, General Marshall is still clinging to his belief that "Europe is more important than Asia" and openly stated that he is unwilling to engage in a "cold war" on two fronts, as if the Asian Chinese side is not worthy of attention. This is where a major crisis is lurking. Our newspaper's editorial will again point out the national nature of communism, which cannot be divided into important and unimportant. The Soviet Union is currently expanding its power simultaneously in Europe and Asia. If the US authorities only know one and not the other, only know the crisis in Europe and not the seriousness of the situation in Asia, then no matter what steps the United States takes, it may not be enough to stop the expansion of communist forces. It must be known that if China falls into the hands of communist rulers, with the entire red China supporting the communist camp, the map of all of Asia will change color, and the United States on the other side of the Pacific may not be able to sleep soundly. Therefore, President Truman's two speeches did not mention China, which is on the front line of anti-communism, and we really cannot help but express our regrets. We would like to reiterate to the American government and the public that the policy of Europe first and Asia later will indeed lead to irreparable disasters. If we do not quickly change course, we will inevitably repeat the mistakes and make a historical mistake!

(Top picture) The new Chilean Ambassador to China, Blanco, presents his credentials to Chairman Chiang. (Bottom picture) The Chilean Ambassador chats with Foreign Minister Wang after presenting his credentials in the National Government Hall. (Taken by Lizhi Society)

27 of Our Ancient Paintings Returned by the Japanese Government Yesterday, All Treasures of Zhang Xueliang 31

[Central News Agency, Tokyo, 18th] Twenty-seven famous Chinese silk paintings of the Ming and Qing dynasties (totaling fifty-six) looted by Japan were returned to our country on the morning of the 18th. It is said that these are the most precious ancient books that can be found in the country, and were given by Zhang Xueliang to the Shenyang Museum before the Shenyang Incident. After the incident, they were looted by the Japanese and sent to Japan in 1943, re-mounted. They were originally scheduled to be returned to Shenyang after being re-mounted, but due to the sudden end of the war, they were preserved in the Imperial Museum of the National Tokyo Museum. Wu Bannong, head of the Compensation and Return Group of our country's delegation to Japan, said: It is not yet known whether each painting will be returned to Zhang. It is believed that because they are precious and rare, each painting should be regarded as state-owned property. Among the twenty-seven paintings, six are Ming paintings and twenty-one are works from the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, including ink treasures of Zhu Zhishan and Emperor Qianlong. Each painting has bright colors and is mostly of flowers and signed divine images. The marks on the paintings indicate that they were purchased by Zhang Zuolin and Zhang Xueliang from Zhu Qiling, who was the Prime Minister under Yuan Shikai. The paintings will be exhibited at the delegation on March 23 with jade screens, jade vases, etc. recently returned by Japan. Journalists from the Allied countries here have been invited to visit. The date of transporting the paintings back to China has not yet been determined.

China National Aviation Corporation Plane Forced to Land in Zhan Yi, Has Safely Flown to Kunming 32

[Central News Agency, Kunming, 18th] The China National Aviation Corporation flight from Shanghai to Kunming on the 16th, after being forced to land in Zhan Yi that night, had eight male passengers and twenty women and children. Yesterday, a special plane dispatched by the company's Kunming station flew to Zhan Yi to transfer them to Kunming. The plane that was forced to land also flew to Kunming at the same time. According to the passengers, the plane left Shanghai on the morning of the 16th, originally scheduled to fly to Kunming via Hankou and Liuzhou. When they learned that the weather in Liuzhou was bad, they changed their route to fly directly from Hankou. At about 5:00 PM, when they flew over the mountains and valleys of the Yunnan border, the right engine suddenly failed, and they encountered a strong wind and rain. They managed to fly for half an hour, but the fuselage lost its balance, so they threw away dozens of packages of mail and luggage, and continued to fly to Zhan Yi and landed. The situation at the time was extremely critical, but the passengers and crew members were very calm, so they were able to land safely and congratulate each other on their rebirth.

Improvement Planned for Taiwan's Water Conservancy 39

[Our Nanjing Office, 18th dispatch] Shen Baixian, along with Shi Chengxi, an inspector from the Ministry, and He Zhenxing, a technician, and nine others, left Nanjing on the 25th of last month to inspect water conservancy in Taiwan. After spending more than half a month there, they returned to Nanjing on the 18th. Speaking to reporters, Mr. Shen shared his impressions from the inspection, stating: “Since Taiwan came under Japanese rule, they implemented colonial policies, exploiting everything like raising chickens for eggs. They vigorously developed irrigation canals and hydroelectric projects and organized local water conservancy groups to assist in their development. Statistics show that the area of irrigated farmland reached over 530,000 hectares, and the length of flood-control embankments exceeded 400,000 meters. However, in the two years leading up to the victory [end of WWII], Japan, struggling to cope, saw all water conservancy facilities damaged by the excavation of defensive fortifications. By the eve of restoration [of Taiwan to China], the area of farmland lacking irrigation reached approximately 200,000 hectares, and around 40,000 meters of embankments were damaged. After the restoration, with the cooperation of water conservancy personnel from the provincial government and water conservancy groups from various counties, over 20,000 meters of embankments have been repaired, and most of the farmland lacking irrigation has been restored.” Mr. Shen also discussed Taiwan’s water conservancy work plan for the current year, which includes plans to repair over 20,000 meters of embankments before the flood season and to strengthen farmland irrigation projects, etc. The total project costs are estimated at over 4.5 billion Taiwan dollars from the provincial treasury and 1.5 billion Taiwan dollars raised locally. He added that the basic-level staff of Taiwan’s water conservancy organizations are lacking in expertise. During the Japanese occupation, the Japanese only provided Taiwanese with some engineering education and work experience, while Japanese personnel filled the senior technical and management positions. This shortcoming should be improved. In the future, the province’s water conservancy efforts should focus on the entire river basin to achieve comprehensive control.

### Assasin of Xu Shoushang, Gao Wanfu, Sentenced to Death 40

[Our Taipei Office, 18th dispatch] Gao Wanfu, the murderer in the Xu Shoushang case, was sentenced to death by the District Court at 9:00 AM on the 18th, with permanent deprivation of civil rights.

Slow Progress in Returning Plundered Materials from Japan 41

My Suggestions Being Considered to Expedite Progress

[Central News Agency, Tokyo, 18th dispatch] Wu Ban-chen, chairman of our country’s Repatriation and Restitution Committee in Japan, told reporters that the Far Eastern Commission is currently studying our country’s suggestion to adopt a "lenient" restitution policy to facilitate the return of materials. Wu believes that the main reason for the slow progress of the restitution work is the various restrictions imposed by the Far Eastern Commission. The Commission places too much emphasis on evidence, making it impossible for our Commission to claim compensation for a large number of losses where evidence is lacking. For example, during the war, Japan plundered 200 motor vehicles from our country, but due to lack of evidence, we can now only claim the return of four vehicles. It is not surprising that documents are insufficient or missing, as documents that could serve as evidence were partially or completely lost during the war. The second obstacle to the restitution work is the lack of direct contact between the Commission and the Japanese government. Otherwise, the Commission could obtain more clues about the plundered items. Over the past year, the Commission has worked hard, but due to the above reasons, the results obtained are far from what was expected. The Commission's achievements in the past include: the entire equipment of the Yongli Chemical Company, the largest nitric acid manufacturer in our country, with a capacity of 1,500 cubic tons, which was taken from Nanjing to Japan, will soon be shipped back on the Hai'e [Seagull] wheel [ship] sailing to Japan. In addition, some iron statues and iron bells plundered from our country's temples will also be transported back to our country on the same ship. The Guangzhou Paper Mill, which was also completely moved to Hokkaido by Japan, will soon be dismantled and returned. The machinery of the Tianjin Sanjia Ban [Plywood] Company and the Shanghai Parker Davis Factory will also be returned, and the latter will be handed over to the United States. The Commission recently negotiated for the return of some machinery from the South China Iron and Steel Company, which was organized by Zeng Yangfu to manufacture automobiles. Of the 3,000 pieces of machinery from the Northwest Industrial Company, organized by Yan Xishan, that were shipped to Japan, 1,000 pieces have been found and will soon be transported back. Other returned items include four ships, four motor vehicles, 35,000 rare books, and 95,000 ordinary books. Two other warships may also be returned to our country recently.

Measures for Entry and Navigation of Foreign Aircraft; Promulgated and Implemented by the Executive Yuan 46

[Central News Agency, Nanjing, 18th dispatch] The Executive Yuan recently promulgated the "Measures for Entry and Navigation of Foreign Aircraft," which stipulate that the public and military aircraft of countries that are contracting parties to the International Civil Aviation Convention and countries that are not contracting parties to the International Civil Aviation Convention shall be handled in accordance with these measures, unless otherwise stipulated in Chinese and foreign treaties, international conventions to which China is a party, and domestic laws. The main points of the measures are as follows: (1) To enter and navigate in China, foreign aircraft must submit an application form through diplomatic channels to the Air Force Headquarters or the Ministry of Communications, which will then forward it to the Air Force Headquarters for approval and issuance of a navigation permit. The application form should be submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs fifteen days before the aircraft takes off, except in special circumstances. (2) Foreign aircraft entering and navigating in China must carry a navigation permit (except for transit flights), a certificate of nationality registration, licenses for pilots and onboard personnel, a flight log, an onboard radio license, and lists of passengers, cargo, and mail. Their entry and navigation must not exceed 16 kilometers on either side of the designated flight route and must comply with the designated airports for takeoff and landing, and they must be subject to inspection by relevant agencies. They must not fly into prohibited airspace. The use of airfields or equipment within the national territory shall be charged according to regulations, unless specifically permitted to be free of charge. (3) Foreign military aircraft entering or transiting China are limited to those that are disarmed and must not carry carrier pigeons or other contraband, unless specifically permitted by the government. (4) Pilots and accompanying cameras and binoculars should be handed over to the person in charge of the aircraft for safekeeping before flying into the national territory.

Burma Since Independence 55

— Our Reporter Yuan Wenzhong

On January 4, 1948, the Blue Sky White Sun banner flew high over the land of Burma. The Union of Burma, with an area of over 260,000 square miles and a population of over 14 million, was thus freed from the 61-year rule of the British Empire, beginning her new life of independence and autonomy.

Independence Ceremony

On March 11th, Lord Mountbatten and his wife flew from Calcutta to Rangoon. On the 12th, they presided over the ceremony of returning the Burmese throne, completing the final ritual of Burmese independence. The press corps took the first flight of the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) between China and Burma to visit Burma, and it coincided with this event, so we were able to participate in this most precious and exciting moment in Burmese history. The Burmese throne was built in 1875 by King Mindon in Mandalay. It is 30 feet and 10 inches high, gilded, and shaped much like a Chinese paifang. There are steps at the back to go up. In 1885, the British captured Mandalay, and the Burmese king was exiled to Bombay. In 1902, Lord Curzon dismantled the throne, packed it into 36 boxes, and transported it to India, where it was displayed in the Indian Museum until now. After Burma became independent, the throne was shipped back to Rangoon from India in 60 sections on February 6th and reassembled in the hall of what used to be the Governor's Office and is now the Presidential Palace. The ceremony presided over by Mountbatten took place in this city hall. On that day, there were hundreds of people including foreign envoys, guests, and Burmese commissioners participating. The ceremony was very simple, with only Mountbatten and the Burmese President each reading a moving speech. The curtain covering the seats of honor was unveiled by Mountbatten, and at the same time the Burmese national anthem was played, thus the form of Burmese independence was successfully completed. Although Mountbatten was still so handsome, he seemed to carry a tired and indifferent expression throughout the ceremony. It is not difficult for people to understand how this lord, who was performing the task of removing a jewel from the British Empire's crown, felt.

Britain Holds the Trump Card

Thus, Britain officially withdrew from the political stage in Burma, but in military and economic terms, she still holds the invincible trump card. The Anglo-Burmese Defense Agreement signed on August 29, 1947, stipulated that British troops should withdraw as soon as possible and that all military equipment should be transferred to the Burmese government. In addition, both sides agreed that Britain should send a military advisory group of the navy, army, and air force to train the Burmese army. The Burmese government must not accept military advisors from other countries other than Britain. "Both sides'" naval vessels may enter each other's territory with notification, and "both sides'" air force planes may fly over each other's territory with notification. "Both sides'" armies may also enter each other's territory when necessary. This agreement is provisionally valid for three years. In other words, British military power in Burma can be controlled for at least three years. Economically, Burma's largest industries and businesses are still firmly in the hands of the British. Several large companies, such as the Burma Oil Company, the Irrawaddy Flotilla Company, and Steel Brothers & Co., control Burma's industry, shipping, and commerce. Their deep-rooted power cannot be shaken in a short period of time.

Government Personnel

Even so, Burma is finally independent. The current Burmese government claims to be an anti-fascist, left-leaning government. It was originally composed of three political parties: the Socialist Party, the People's Volunteer Organization, and the Communist Party, and was named the Anti-Fascist People's Freedom League (AFPFL). However, after coming to power, the Communist Party withdrew due to disagreements over its political program and split into the Red Flag Communist Party and the White Flag Communist Party. The Red Flag is the most leftist radical party and has now been declared an illegal party by the government. The White Flag is more moderate, but it also refuses to cooperate with the government. In addition, the right-wing opposition parties include the Dobama Asiayone, the Patriotic Party, and the People's Party. In last year's world-shaking Burmese coup, Aung San, chairman of the AFPFL, was assassinated by U Saw, leader of the Patriotic Party. U Saw was recently sentenced to death by the court. Prime Minister Thakin Nu, the vice-chairman of the AFPFL, holds the actual power.

Clarifying Policies

Regarding the current government's policies, Thakin Nu elaborated in detail at the Constituent Assembly. He said: "Why should Burma go to the left? Because Burma's wealth is completely concentrated in the hands of the first British, second Indian, and third Chinese capitalists. The Burmese common people live in the lowest level of poverty, gnawing on the bones left by others. This kind of unfair situation must be eliminated, but its meaning is not to create a small number of Burmese capitalists to replace the British, Indian, and Chinese capitalists, while the majority of the people remain poor and suffering. Therefore, the government's policy is to establish a system that benefits all the people, so that all the people can enjoy its benefits. This policy is not radical, and it cannot be successful overnight. This policy is not completely Soviet-style either, because Burma's geographical environment is not as close to the Soviet Union as Czechoslovakia or Bulgaria. The most important task of the Burmese government today is to do its utmost to make the country strong. Only when the country is stronger can we move further forward!"

Economic Status Quo

Indeed, until now, Burma's wealth is completely in the hands of the British, Indians, and Chinese. The British are far above, while the Indians and Overseas Chinese hold the middle and lower levels of industry and commerce. In the downtown area of Rangoon, it is simply the world of the British, Indians, and Overseas Chinese. It is rare to see shops opened by Burmese people. The Burmese government is now striving to move towards national economic socialism. It announced a real estate law prohibiting the sale or mortgage of real estate in Burma to foreigners, but this only affects the Overseas Chinese, while British and Indian residents can still be an exception. It also controls import and export trade, stipulating that 50 percent of the quota should be given to Burmese merchants, but because the Burmese merchants themselves do not have this ability, they either transfer the license or cooperate with foreigners, so the results are still obtained by foreign merchants. It also wants to nationalize the mining industry, but because of financial difficulties, it cannot afford to pay the purchase price, so it is unlikely to be realized in the near future. Marshall Emphasizes the Need to Strengthen Military Strength, Urges Congress to Make Decisions and Take Action, Military Leaders Also Attend Senate to Testify 56

[Our Report] New York, 18th Broadcast: Washington News, Secretary of Defense Forrestal and Secretary of the Army Royal presented their views to the Senate Armed Services Committee today, advocating for an increase in the currently stipulated military strength and strongly supporting President Truman's proposed implementation of universal conscription and temporary restoration of [the] draft. Mr. Chen [Forrestal] stated that the current stipulated military strength is based on assumptions made two years ago, which have not been realized. He did not provide exact figures but said that definite recommendations could only be made after detailed research. Mr. Forrestal stated that the stipulated strength of the Army is 669,000, but there are only 560,000 people currently serving; the stipulated strength of the Navy is 664,000, and only 474,000 are currently serving; the stipulated strength of the Air Force is 471,000, and only 362,000 are currently serving. These figures show that the current shortage is 400,800 people. However, Mr. Forrestal previously estimated the shortage to be 350,000 people. Congressional Republican leaders remain lukewarm to universal conscription, but they are not overly opposed to implementing a new draft. Mr. Forrestal strongly argued that we must not hold the view that the existence of atomic bombs means that a large number of personnel are no longer needed.

[US Information Service, Washington, 17th dispatch] After President Truman requested Congress today to re-establish conscription and formulate universal conscription, Secretary of State Marshall issued a statement urging Congress to take decisive action to show "America's determination to maintain a strong strength to maintain peace and freedom in the European world." Secretary Marshall made this statement to the Senate Military Committee. The Committee began public discussions today on the issue of universal conscription and on the President's request to restore the draft and increase the strength of the national armed forces to an appropriate level. The universal conscription bill has been successfully reported in the House Military Committee, but the House Rules Committee has not yet presented the bill on the floor.

[Associated Press, Washington, 17th dispatch] Secretary of State Marshall testified before the Senate Military Committee today that without military strength, diplomatic actions in the current world situation can only lead to appeasement. The Committee should discuss the National Youth Military Training Act and the Temporary Conscription Act, and the US Air Force expansion program also needs to be considered. Mr. Marshall said that the temporary Conscription Act is the only way to quickly replenish the troops to full strength. In the case of Korea, the garrison commander requested an increase in troops to 38,000, but the Army Department only sent 30,000, and even that number could not be fully deployed due to personnel shortages. On February 8 of this year, there were a total of 18,000 troops stationed in Korea, and recent reports show that there are only 15,000 troops, and this garrison is still shrinking. Mr. Marshall also said that the Italian elections on the 18th of this month are far more important than local events in that country. This move will not only determine whether Italy can restore true democracy but will also foreshadow a trend of division, which may extend to the shores of the Atlantic.

[United Press, Washington, 17th dispatch] The US Army Department revealed on the 17th that it is drafting a plan to restore the Selective Service System based on President Truman's request to Congress to approve a temporary conscription system to help curb the spread of the Soviet Union.

On President Truman's Policy Declaration: Western European Nations Express Welcome; Moscow Indicates Political Motivation 57

[United Press International, London, 18th] Western European nations unanimously praised President Truman's message as a "New Monroe Doctrine," providing a basis for the European Recovery Program. The number of people listening to the message, from the Arctic Ocean to Africa, broke all previous records, and its acclaim was unprecedented since the war. Moscow Radio, exceptionally, broadcast Truman's message to the entire Soviet population in the early morning.

[Our Newspaper Report] London, 18th Broadcast: Moscow claims that President Truman deliberately created a crisis in his speech yesterday to serve his party's interests.

[Reuters, London, 17th] Diplomatic circles here feel that President Truman's call for Congress to reinstate conscription, implement universal military training, and quickly pass the aid to Europe bill implies a military guarantee for the five-nation Western European Union treaty. The consolidation of the global anti-communist front has achieved unprecedented success in the past 24 hours. Following the agreement by sixteen European nations in Paris yesterday to establish a permanent economic cooperation organization, the UK, France, Netherlands, Belgium, and Luxembourg formed a military mutual assistance pact in Brussels today. Ninety minutes later, President Truman in Washington frankly expressed his willingness to provide Western European countries with any needed military assistance. This series of significant actions occurring within a short 24 hours is truly rare in history.

[Reuters, Paris, 17th] President Truman's speech to Congress has made a profound and significant impression on French officials and the public. While it was generally expected that Truman would make a strong statement, few anticipated such specific recommendations and such blatant warnings to the Soviet Union. It is also believed here that Truman's support for the Western European five-nation pact is tantamount to declaring that in the event of the circumstances described in the five-nation pact, and the five nations engage in self-defense, the United States will participate in military intervention. The US President's particular emphasis on affirmative and proactive action, rather than just verbal intimidation of the Soviet Union, is especially welcomed by responsible officials here.

[Associated Press, London, 17th] Western Europe unanimously expressed admiration for Truman's declaration tonight. In Rome, government officials believe that Truman's speech is highly relevant to Italy. In The Hague, the Dutch Foreign Ministry considers it a great encouragement to Western Europe.

Positive Reaction from US Congressional Leaders 58

[Reuters, Washington, 17th] A senior US official told our agency that Truman's decision to request the reinstatement of conscription was significantly influenced by British Foreign Secretary Bevin. After Bevin informed Marshall that verbal protests alone were insufficient to halt communist expansion and would only demonstrate the West's impotence, US Ambassador to the Soviet Union Smith was the first to propose the reinstatement of conscription. Senator Vandenberg, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, stated, "Truman's speech is a speech for peace. If domestic communists attempt to rely on foreign support to undermine domestic unity, the speech will become a speech for war." Republican Senator Taft stated, "Truman has made clear his and our unified determination to prevent the expansion of communism as much as possible." Representative Eaton, Chairman of the House Foreign Affairs Committee, stated that he would do everything possible to meet Truman's request for the swift passage of the European Recovery Program. Meanwhile, the Senate Armed Services Committee announced that it would begin reviewing the conscription and universal military training requests immediately, with Secretary of State Marshall being the first to testify.

UK and Transjordan Sign New Treaty of Alliance 59

Emphasis on Military Mutual Assistance

[Associated Press, London, 17th] The new treaty of alliance signed by the UK and Transjordan in Amman last Monday was announced here today, stipulating that if one of the signatory countries is at war or faces a threat of war, it may request the other party to send troops to assist. The UK may establish two air force bases in Transjordan and may train troops. The UK and Transjordan shall form a joint defense committee to determine the location of British troops stationed there. The UK agrees to supply Transjordan with military equipment, arms, aircraft, and other materials, and agrees to provide financial assistance to the King of Transjordan. The UK agrees to send officers to train the Transjordanian army. The treaty is valid for twenty years.

Czech Coup Case Added to Security Council Agenda 60

Chilean Representative Invited to Attend and Present Arguments

[Central News Agency, Lake Success, 17th] The Security Council, disregarding the strong opposition from the Soviet Union and Ukraine, began discussing the case in which the former Czech representative accused the Soviet Union of manipulating the Czech coup. The Security Council voted nine to two to include in the Council's agenda the accusation that the Soviet Union manipulated the Czech coup, which was initially proposed by former Czech representative Papánek and formally supported by the Chilean government. The Security Council also voted nine to two (with the Soviet Union and Ukraine voting against) to invite the Chilean representative to attend the meeting and state their recommendations.

The Security Council decided today, after nearly two hours of debate in an unprecedented atmosphere of tension, to consider this highly explosive Czech issue. The public gallery of the Security Council was packed today, and emotions ran high during the proceedings. The Chairman of the Security Council, our representative Jiang Tingfu, repeatedly tried to suppress cheers and applause.

[Associated Press, Washington, 17th] The House Foreign Affairs Committee today, in a closed-door meeting, approved the $5.3 billion Aid to Europe Bill, stipulating that $1 billion of this amount will be loaned by the Export-Import Bank. Truman Delivers Political Speech, Severely Criticizes Wallace - At the St. Patrick's Day Banquet 63

Truman's words were met with thunderous applause from the audience. Truman's tenure as president has been a time of many troubles, and this criticism of Wallace has brought matters to a climax. Wallace has been highly critical of Truman's foreign policy, and he sent a telegram to congressional leaders on the 17th stating that the government was inciting "war hysteria." Wallace is scheduled to broadcast on Thursday evening to respond to Truman's congressional message, and is sure to respond to Truman's statement about "communists." Truman and his party boarded a special train on the evening of the 17th and are expected to return to Washington on Thursday morning.

It is an alliance formed by like-minded neighboring countries seeking closer social and spiritual unity. Its principles are in line with Britain's good neighbor policy and are definitely not directed at any other country.

Full Text of Truman's Speech 70

[From the United States News Agency, Washington, 17th] The full text of Truman's speech is as follows: "I am here today to report to you on the seriousness of the situation in Europe and to suggest actions for your consideration: Europe is undergoing rapid changes, which will affect our foreign policy and our national security. For those nations striving to maintain a form of government that grants freedom to the people, there is now an increasing threat. The United States is deeply concerned about the preservation of these nations' freedom. To maintain the conditions under which we can achieve a lasting peace based on freedom and justice, we must take action now. Achieving this peace has always been the great goal of our country.

Almost three years have passed since the end of the greatest war in history, yet peace and stability have not returned to the world. We know that the end of the war does not automatically solve the problems it caused. Building peace after a war has always been a difficult task. Even if all the Allied nations in World War II shared a common desire to build a just and honorable peace, there were still enormous difficulties in reaching this goal.

But today's world situation is not primarily the result of the natural difficulties that arise after a war. It is mainly due to one nation that has not only refused to cooperate in establishing a just and honorable peace but—worse—has actively worked to prevent it.

Congress is very familiar with the progress of the situation.

You know that democratic countries have sincerely and patiently attempted to find a solid foundation for peace through negotiations and agreements. Conferences have been held time and again in different parts of the world. We have tried to resolve the problems caused by the war on a basis that would allow a fair peace to be established. You know the difficulties we have encountered, but the past record stands like a monument, upright, proving the loyalty and integrity of the world's democracies. The agreements we have reached, though not perfect, can provide a basis for a fair peace—provided that these agreements are observed.

But the agreements have not been observed.

These agreements have been repeatedly scorned and violated by one nation.

Congress is also very familiar with the development of the United Nations. The majority of the world's nations have united within the United Nations, striving to establish a world order based on law rather than force. The majority of nations warmly and sincerely support the United Nations and are working to make it stronger and more effective.

But one nation has repeatedly abused the veto power, obstructing the work of the United Nations. In the period of two years and some months, this nation has vetoed twenty-one proposed actions.

But that is not enough. Since the end of the war, the Soviet Union and its agents have destroyed the independence and democratic character of a series of countries in Eastern and Central Europe.

It is this brutal action and the apparent attempt to extend this action to the remaining free nations of Europe that have created today's crisis in Europe.

The fall of the Czech Republic has shocked the entire civilized world. Pressure is now being applied to Finland, making the Scandinavian Peninsula precarious. Greece is under direct military attack by traitors, who are actively supported by communist-controlled neighboring countries. In Italy, a communist minority is desperately trying to control the country. Although the methods used vary, the pattern is very clear.

Amid this growing threat, there are now encouraging signs that the free nations of Europe are becoming more united for their economic well-being and the common defense of their freedom.

In the economic sphere, mutual aid efforts are underway to restore the conditions necessary to preserve free institutions. In Paris, the sixteen nations cooperating in the European Recovery Program are now meeting again, establishing a joint organization to work for the economic recovery of Western Europe.

The United States firmly supports these nations' efforts to repair the damage caused by the war and restore a healthy world economy. When I presented this plan to Congress last December, I emphasized the need for prompt action. Since that day, everything in Europe has clearly indicated the extreme urgency of taking such steps.

The Soviet Union and its satellite countries were invited to participate in the European Recovery Program. They refused this invitation. Moreover, they declared their fierce hostility to the program and attempted to undermine it with an aggressive posture. They see in this plan a major obstacle to achieving their attempt to subdue the free societies of Europe. They do not even want the sixteen cooperating nations to practice self-help.

The economic recovery of Europe is essential, but economic reconstruction measures alone are not enough. The free nations of Europe understand that if economic recovery is to succeed, some means of protection must be provided against domestic and foreign aggression. As the threats to their freedom have increased, a movement for collective self-defense has accompanied the movement for economic cooperation.

At this very moment as I speak to you, five nations of the free societies of Europe are signing a fifty-year agreement in Brussels for economic cooperation and joint defense against aggression.

This action is of great importance because this agreement was not imposed by a more powerful neighbor. It represents the choice of independent governments representing the will of the people and is being undertaken in accordance with the provisions stipulated in the Charter of the United Nations.

Its significance far outweighs the actual provisions of the agreement itself. It is an important step on Europe's path to unity in order to defend and preserve its civilization. This development deserves our full support. I believe that the United States will extend its support to free nations in appropriate ways as the situation requires. I believe that the determination of the free nations of Europe to protect themselves will be matched by our own determination to help them do so.

Recent developments in Europe have made us aware of many basic questions of great importance.

I believe we have reached the point where the position of the United States must be stated without error.

The principles and goals in the United Nations Charter still represent our hope for establishing law in international relations. This charter constitutes the international ethic. The basic form of discipline, and this international ethic is what our country believes in. But we cannot ignore the cruel fact that, due to the obstruction and even contempt of one country, this great dream has not yet been fully realized.

Therefore, we must take other measures to supplement the work of the United Nations and support its goals. In the history of the world, sometimes action is wiser than hesitation. Action, of course, contains certain risks, but the risk of inaction is greater. Because if we act wisely now, we will strengthen the United Nations and the forces of freedom, justice, and peace represented by all the free nations of the world.

Therefore, I consider it my responsibility to make recommendations to Congress, which, in my judgment, are best suited to support all free and democratic nations in Europe and improve the foundation of our own national strength.

First, I suggest that Congress swiftly complete its action on the European Recovery Program. This program is the foundation of our policy of aid to Europe. Its rapid passage is the most effective contribution we can make to peace.

The Senate's resolute action, regardless of political issues, is a remarkable example of the effective work of democracy.

Time is of great importance now. I am very excited to hear the news that the House plans to take swift action. I hope not a day will be wasted. Second, I suggest the swift enactment of legislation for universal military training.

Until the free nations of Europe regain their strength, and as long as the threat of communism to the survival of democracy persists, the United States must maintain sufficient strength to support those European nations threatened by communist control and police state rule.

I believe we have learned the importance of maintaining military strength to prevent war. We have discovered that if we want to maintain peace in peacetime, a sound military system is necessary. In the past, aggressors, seeing our apparent lack of military power, have unwisely precipitated wars. Although they were ultimately destroyed by misunderstanding our strength, we have paid a terrible price for being unprepared.

Universal military training is the only acceptable way to build up the civilian personnel of our armed forces to a level sufficient to meet emergencies. Our ability to mobilize a large number of trained personnel in times of emergency can prevent future conflicts, and this ability, combined with other measures of national policy, can restore stability to the world.

The United States' adoption of universal military training at this time will clearly demonstrate to the world our determination to support the will to seek peace with the strength to seek peace. I believe that the American people, through Congress, will decide to adopt universal military training, which is crucial to encouraging every free government in the world.

Third, I suggest the temporary re-enactment of conscription legislation to maintain adequate strength in our armed forces.

Our armed forces lack the personnel necessary to maintain adequate strength. Although the strength of the armed forces has been reduced to the minimum necessary to meet overseas obligations, far below the minimum it should be on the American mainland, our armed forces cannot maintain their proper strength through voluntary enlistment.

Unless we maintain our armed forces, we cannot fulfill our international responsibilities, such as maintaining our occupying forces in Germany until peace and stability are achieved in Europe.

There is no conflict between the need for conscription in the regular army and universal training in the reserves. Conscription is necessary until the foundation of universal training is laid, at which point conscription can be terminated and the regular army can be maintained on the basis of volunteers.

The proposals I have made represent the most urgent steps to achieve peace and prevent war.

We must be prepared to take all wise and necessary steps to achieve this great goal. This will require us to provide assistance to other countries. It will also require adequate and well-coordinated military strength. We must be prepared to pay the price of peace, or we can be sure that we will pay the price of war.

We in America remain determined to seek a just and honorable basis for resolving international disputes in every possible way. We will continue to be loyal to the United Nations and use it as the primary means of achieving international security based on law rather than force. We will always be ready and eager to cooperate with other nations—I repeat, with all nations—to achieve international understanding in every possible endeavor.

For the Soviet Union and any other country willing to cooperate sincerely to preserve peace, this door has never been closed, and it will not be closed in the future.

At the same time, we must not be confused about the central problem facing the world today.

The time has come when the free men and women of the world must bravely face the threats to their freedom.

The United States has a great responsibility to act for the welfare of the world based on our strength. We have learned that we must obtain the peace we seek through genuine effort and not through illusion, just as we fought for victory in war. At no time in our history has the unity of our people been more important than now.

To fully shoulder the tasks before us, unity of purpose, unity of effort, and unity of spirit are essential.

Everyone here today has a special responsibility. The situation in the world is so critical, and the responsibilities of this country are so great, that partisan strife cannot be allowed to diminish our influence in maintaining peace.

The American people have the right to assume that political issues will not affect our common work. They have the right to assume that in our efforts to maintain world peace, we will move forward hand in hand with all our might and without hesitation. With the help of God, we will succeed." (End)

The City's Request to Reduce Conscription Quota Denied / Reasons for Deferment of Draftees Occur After Review / Applications for Supplementary Deferment Review Permitted 71

[Report from this newspaper] The city's initial conscription this year involves 6,000 men. The Civil Affairs Bureau, citing the city's status as an industrial and commercial area, previously requested the city government to forward a request to the National Government to reduce the quota by 1,000 men this year. Yesterday, a telegram from the National Government rejected the request, stating that the city's conscription quota for the 37th year had already been reduced, being lower than the ratio for any other province (or city), so the requested reduction would not be approved.

[Another report] Regarding the review of applications for exemption or deferment of military service for eligible men in the city, this was completed at the end of last year. However, if the reasons for deferment arise after the review, supporting documents can still be submitted for a temporary supplementary review for deferment. However, those suspected of evasion are excluded. Recently, the Civil Affairs Bureau has received numerous letters requesting deferment based on the above circumstances, and supplementary reviews will be conducted.

Military Service Propaganda Meeting to be Held on the 26th 72

Three Days of Expanded Propaganda for Suppressing Rebellion and Building the Nation

[Report from this newspaper] The military service propaganda meeting, to be held at the Queen's Grand Theater at 9:00 AM on the 22nd, is currently being actively prepared. Staff of British Tram Company Staged a Work Stoppage Yesterday 73

[Report from this newspaper] Interior staff of the British Tram Company staged a "petition by work stoppage" yesterday morning. This was because the labor union had previously submitted four demands to the company's management. After mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, the company accepted three of the demands, but a resolution on the issue of year-end salary increases for staff could not be reached. As a result, the staff felt that the authorities were deliberately discriminating against them and expressed great dissatisfaction. They then decided to petition individually. The chairman of the labor union, Qiu Changjiang, and others tried their best to dissuade them but were unsuccessful. Therefore, the standing director Chen Chunbao and seven staff representatives went to the Social Affairs Bureau. The deputy director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Zhao, personally received them and urged them to resume work immediately. As for the issue of year-end salary increases, the bureau scheduled a meeting with both labor and management at 10:00 AM this morning to mediate. The petitioning staff complied and resumed work in full at 1:00 PM in the afternoon, making up for the work missed in the morning.

Situation of Haihu Ship Improves / Additional Jian Lun Sent for Rescue 79

[Report from this newspaper] The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haihu ship ran aground in the waters of Xia Dou, with a serious situation. The headquarters continuously dispatched ships for rescue, and various developments have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, according to reliable information from the company, the location where the Haihu ship ran aground is near Jinmen Island, where the previous Haizhe ship ran aground. In the past few days, the ship's power was cut off, and radio communication was lost, so there was no news. Now it is known that the situation has improved, and the Min 302 tugboat has arrived at the scene of the accident. The Xiamen branch has also dispatched multiple barges and is trying to unload the cargo in the cabin. Furthermore, the Jian Lun, which was transferred from Qingdao for rescue, has arrived in Shanghai yesterday and is scheduled to sail to Xiamen today to assist in the towing and rescue. According to Captain Fan Lun of the Jian Lun, if there is no change in the sea climate, the rescue work can be carried out smoothly. It was also stated that the Jian Lun was originally in Qingdao to rescue the Mingxing ship of the Zhongxing Company, which ran aground after hitting a reef. Initially, the stern of the ship sank, and rescue seemed hopeless. Recently, the ship's body suddenly leveled, and there is a possibility of escaping the danger. However, this ship urgently needed to go to Xiamen to rescue the Haihu ship, so the insurance company that underwrote the Mingxing ship has hired technicians to try to rescue it.

Passengers Transferred from Xiamen to Shantou and then to Guangzhou 80

[Report from this newspaper, Xiamen, 18th] After the Haihu ship ran aground near Jinmen Island, various naval vessels that came to Xiamen for rescue were unable to get close due to their deep draft, so it has not yet been freed from danger. Currently, one-third of the ship's body is grounded on the reef. As for the more than 130 passengers who arrived in Xiamen, they will be transported by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Dabeiyun to Shantou this afternoon and then transferred to Guangzhou.

Household Registration Transfers Still Handled by the Civil Affairs Bureau 82

Regarding the registration of household registration transfers in the city, which was originally handled by the Civil Affairs Bureau, the Ministry of the Interior recently requested the city government to transfer it to the Police Bureau. However, the City Council resolved in a general meeting that this was inconsistent with the law and has telegraphed the central government to withdraw the order. The City Council further telegraphed the Civil Affairs Bureau yesterday that the management agency should remain as it was before the central government issued a reply order. At the same time, it also sent a letter to the city government ordering the Civil Affairs Bureau to handle the matters in accordance with the Household Registration Law. The Police Bureau should assign police officers to assist in the investigation and recording of transfers. The Civil Affairs Bureau has now notified all districts to accept applications for household registration transfers as usual and not to evade responsibility.

Next Month Allotted Rice Will Be American Rice; Rice Ration Coupons to Be Distributed on the 26th; Rice Market Should Employ Purchase Policies 88

[Our Reporter] The People's Food Allocation Committee of this city has decided that the rice ration coupons for April, which are sold based on population, will be sent to the district offices on March 25th and distributed by the 26th. It is hoped that all citizens will be able to receive their ration coupons by the end of the month. All the rice allotted next month will be American relief rice, and the quality is very good. The Allocation Committee is preparing to start delivering rice to various rice retailers on March 28th, starting with one-third, totaling 170,000 shih, before the end of the month. It is expected that citizens will be able to purchase the allotted rice with their coupons at the beginning of April.

[Our Reporter] Since the implementation of the comprehensive rice rationing in this city from March to date, the amount of rationed rice released from the warehouses has reached 350,000 shih. It is estimated that this figure accounts for about 50% of the city's total monthly demand for rice, which has greatly affected the rice sales in the market. The North and South Rice Markets specifically petitioned the People's Food Allocation Committee, claiming that the market has been sluggish in recent weeks, and prices have repeatedly fallen, even below the production area. This has led to a gradual decrease in arrivals. If this phenomenon continues, it will inevitably make the city's reserves even more empty. Therefore, they requested the People's Food Allocation Committee to implement a purchase policy, entrusting the management committees of the North and South Rice Markets to conduct the purchases on their behalf. This request will be submitted to the municipal meeting for discussion by Chairman Ren.

Four Boxes of Contraband Goods Seized at Wusong Bus Station; Suspected of Being Transported to Communist-Controlled Areas 89

[Our Reporter] At around 3:00 PM on the afternoon of the 11th, a car suddenly drove into the Wusong Wai Ma Lu Bus Station and unloaded four wooden boxes. A person stood beside them, looking like he was waiting for transshipment. Lou Qishui, a police officer on duty at the Wusong Police Station, went forward to ask what was in the boxes. He was told they were cigarettes, and the officer left. Glancing back, he saw that the man looked suspicious, so he turned back and interrogated him, and opened the boxes. As expected, he found a large number of cigarettes, and after removing the cigarette packaging, he discovered that they were all Western medicines and photographic materials. He took them all to the station. The man confessed that his name was Lin Zhigao, from Chongming, and that a friend had asked him to take the items to Chongming to sell. The station deemed the goods to be prohibited exports, fearing that they would flow into the communist-controlled areas, and immediately detained him. The case was then submitted to the Municipal Police Bureau for investigation the next day.

Lan Chunchi Accused of Illegally Allocating Trucks; Supervisory Committee Member Zheng Zhongwu Testifies 90

The District Procuratorate summoned Zheng Zhongwu, the chairman of the "Fu-Pu-Xian Automobile Transportation Company," who is also a Supervisory Committee member and National Assembly representative, to testify. Zheng, who had passed through Shanghai from Min to Beijing to attend the National Assembly, reported to the District Procuratorate to testify. According to Zheng's testimony, he was the founder and chairman of the "Fu-Pu-Xian Automobile Transportation Company," which was later changed to the Putian Private Automobile Company. However, the company is now closed. During his tenure as chairman, he applied to the Executive Yuan for two trucks and sent employees Chen Qing and Lin Yimei to Shanghai to pick them up. He was not very clear about the details. Chen has now gone to Southeast Asia, and Lin is still in Putian, it is said. The prosecutor, seeking to clarify the truth, will summon Lin for questioning.

Many Spring Outings; Railway Bureau Adds Trains on Sundays 93

Due to the large number of people going on spring outings, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Bureaus expect that passenger traffic on the two lines will be very crowded on Saturdays and Sundays. They recently decided to add a first-class reserved-seat car to the No. 72 special express train departing from Shanghai to Wuxi at 8:30 AM on Sunday mornings. This was trialed for the past two weeks, but most passengers still preferred to purchase tickets for the Triumph Express departing from Shanghai at 8:00 AM, resulting in the Triumph Express often being fully booked, while the No. 72 train, which departed half an hour later, was very empty. The Railway Bureau hopes that passengers traveling from Shanghai to Suzhou and Wuxi in the future can take the 8:30 AM special express train to avoid difficulties in purchasing tickets.

Murder Conviction of Zhan Zhou Shi Who Killed Her Husband Overturned 94

Zhan Zhou Shi, the protagonist of the sensational case during the enemy-puppet period, who killed her husband with eighteen knife wounds, was sentenced to death by the enemy-puppet court. At that time, the famous female writer Su Qing wrote an article to defend her, appealing for justice. After the victory, the Shanghai District Court initiated a retrial and still sentenced her to death. Zhan Zhou Shi, dissatisfied with the sentence, hired lawyer Shi Baixiu to file an appeal. The High Court has now ruled to overturn the original sentence and change it to fifteen years of imprisonment.

Shanxi Field and Grain Director, etc., Pass Through Shanghai to Beijing to Request Emergency Food Aid from the Central Government 95

[Our Reporter] The Shanxi Provincial Government, considering the serious food shortage in the province urgently in need of relief, dispatched Guan Minquan, Director of the Department of Construction, Geng Shi, Director of the Field and Grain Department, Liang Xianwu, Director of the Department of Social Affairs, Yin Yulan, Counselor of the Provincial Government, and He Defu, a member of the Provincial Assembly, yesterday from Ping by plane to Shanghai. They planned to take the train to Beijing that evening to visit the relevant authorities to present the real situation of the food shortage in Shanxi.

Allocation of 20,000 Tons of Grain to Be Transported in Seven Months

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, they hosted reporters from various newspapers in the city on the fifth floor of the Bankers' Association. Geng Shi first reported the purpose of going to Beijing, saying: The food shortage in Shanxi Province is serious. Chairman Yan has previously telegraphed Chairman Chiang and Premier Zhang separately to request relief, and concrete solutions have been obtained. Therefore, this trip to Beijing is not in the nature of a petition. It is only intended to make a detailed presentation to the central government on the actual difficulties in local food supply. The Shanxi Provincial Government initially requested the central government to allocate 30,000 tons of food. Now, considering the actual situation, it plans to request the central government to allocate a minimum of 5,000 tons of relief grain and 5,000 tons of regulatory grain. In addition, it will request loans from the Four Joint Offices and ask the Ministry of Food to purchase 10,000 tons, totaling 20,000 tons. Using ten airplanes, operating twice a day, it will take about seven months to transport it. The Shanxi Provincial Government is currently investigating the amount of wild vegetables to be used as supplementary food. At the same time, it has implemented a food reduction program, distributing the food for four people to five people.

Each Bag of Flour Costs as Much as Six Million

He Defu then delivered a speech, saying: Currently, the communist army in Shanxi Province maintains a force of more than 100,000 troops, constantly harassing the area, and transportation has been cut off. Moreover, among the 3.6 million people in central Shanxi, more than 600,000 refugees have been forced to flee to safe areas due to the communist "locust policy". Furthermore, last year's drought was followed by floods, which is the biggest reason for the current food shortage in central Shanxi. Currently, each bag of flour in Taiyuan costs more than 6 million yuan, each dan of millet costs 11 million yuan, and each jin of sorghum costs 80,000 yuan, and there is nowhere to buy it. Previously, the Shanxi Provincial Government could exchange one piece of No. 3 coarse cloth for one dan and three dou and six sheng of wheat from the people, but now it is impossible to exchange even five dou. It is estimated that in the next three months, on average, 40% of the people in central Shanxi will not be able to obtain food. The situation has reached an extremely serious stage. Therefore, it is urged that the central government quickly allocate food and strengthen air transport to alleviate the urgent need. Otherwise, it is also proposed to request the central government to grant loans to purchase and transport food from the provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan. At the same time, it is hoped that the public opinion circles will provide enthusiastic support. The reception ended at 5:30 PM.

Wu Zhide Arrested for Defrauding Diamond Ring at Deda Hotel 96

[Our Reporter] Wu Zhide, 25 years old, from Suzhou, who runs a rice business, is staying in room 428 of the Da Zhonghua Hotel. At about 1:00 PM the day before yesterday, he went to the Central Market on Sichuan Road, holding a diamond ring worth about 15 million yuan and loudly offering it for sale. Many people gathered to watch. Soon, a swindler named Tong Shi'ren approached him, falsely claiming that the manager of the Deda Hotel wanted to buy it. He took the diamond ring to the entrance of the Deda Hotel and told Wu to wait for a moment. Unexpectedly, the swindler entered through the front door and exited through the back door, disappearing without a trace. More than half an hour later, Wu realized that he had been defrauded and went to the Huopu Police Station to report it. Li Yinmin, the section chief, ordered officers Ren Fengwu and Zhou Xueqin, the police chief, to wait in the area of the Central Market the next afternoon. They finally arrested the swindler Tong Shi'ren and brought him to the branch office, where he confessed to the fraud. It has been decided to submit the case to the District Procuratorate today for investigation.

Price Fluctuation Statistics; Rice Rose the Least, Stocks Rose the Most 97

[Our Reporter] According to a survey by the Municipal People's Food Allocation Committee, the price fluctuations of various important commodities in the city from February 28th to the 16th of this month are listed for comparison. Bai Geng rose by 13.3%, Xian rice rose by 9.5%, 20-count Double Horse yarn rose by 20.9%, Longtou fine cloth rose by 32.6%, Yongsha stocks rose by 68.4%, and Gubenzao soap rose by 12.9%. The person in charge of the Allocation Committee analyzed the above statistics, believing that the increase in the price of rice was the smallest, approximately equal to the black market interest rate, and Xian rice was even lower than the interest rate, which proves that the rice rationing policy has been effective. Due to the sluggish sales in the rice market, idle capital has been concentrated in stocks and other markets. Therefore, it is believed that suppressing prices requires coordinated efforts to achieve significant results.

Execution of Seizure of Enemy-Puppet Property Changed to Judicial Organs; Provisional Measures for the Disposal of Traitorous Property Abolished 100

The Enemy-Puppet Property Clearing Office previously submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to change the matters entrusted to the office for the execution of seizure and attachment of traitorous property to be handled by the judicial organs themselves. The Executive Yuan has now approved the implementation of this request, and the provisional measures previously formulated for the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District and the Shanghai-Nanjing Municipal High Procuratorates to entrust the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Anhui District Enemy-Puppet Property Handling Bureau to execute the seizure, confiscation, and disposal of traitorous property have been abolished. From now on, the seizure of traitorous property will be executed by the competent judicial organs themselves in accordance with the law, or entrusted to the enemy-puppet property handling organs or local administrative organs for execution in accordance with the law. The custody and confiscation of traitorous property shall be handled in accordance with the "Joint Measures for the Execution of Confiscation of Traitorous Property" issued by the Yuan and the five key points for handling the property of traitors in other counties as instructed by the Yuan. The office yesterday issued a circular to its branches in various places to comply with and handle the matter, and also sent a letter to the Shanghai High Procuratorate to comply with the order and handle it itself from today onwards.
