Newspaper Economy Implemented Next Month; Those with More Than One and a Half Sheets Will Be Reduced by Half a Sheet 105

[Our Reporter] Wu Kaixian, Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs, and Yuan Wenzhang, Director of the Fourth Division, invited those in charge of various newspapers in the city to a discussion yesterday afternoon. During the meeting, Director Wu relayed the central government's regulations on saving paper. After exchanging views with those in charge of various newspapers, it was agreed to comply with the central government's order to reduce the size of the newspapers. From April 1st, newspapers in the city with more than one and a half sheets will each be reduced by half a sheet. The Yishi Daily and the Shang Bao originally had two large sheets. After the central government's paper saving order arrived, they automatically reduced to one and a half sheets. Therefore, they will maintain the original one and a half sheet size this time. Various newspapers hope that the central government will continue to allocate the original quota for the fifth allocation of paper.

Emergency First Aid Station Established; Ceremony Just Ended; Immediately Called Out 106

The "Shanghai Nursing Ten," the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Emergency First Aid Station, which was organized by the Police Bureau's Fire Department in a short period of time, held a simple and solemn establishment ceremony at the department yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, announcing its official establishment and commencement of service. The ceremony was presided over by Zhou Zhaoxiang, who is also the chief stationmaster, and Wang Hanmei, deputy chief stationmaster, Ye Binyong, chief of the Fire Department's First Aid Section, and the fire chiefs of various fire districts were all present. Police Bureau Chief Yu Shuping delivered a training speech at about 10:00 AM, stating: "The Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Emergency First Aid Station, like the Flying Fortress and the Mobile Police Station, can be called sister flowers. The first aid station is limited by funding, so it will first set up three sub-stations, and will strive to expand in the future. Nurses and paramedics in the first aid station should aim to serve the citizens and win the praise of all sectors to bring glory to the police." Zhou, who is also the chief stationmaster, then gave a training speech to encourage them. The ceremony ended at 11:00 AM. There are currently ten service nurses and forty paramedic police officers. The nurses all wear white work clothes, white socks, white leather shoes, and white nurse caps, with the words "Shanghai Police Bureau" in blue and "Shanghai Nurse" in red embroidered on the pocket of their chest. The paramedic police officers all wear red cross armbands. When the "Shanghai Nurses" are dispatched for first aid, they will issue a postcard to each patient's family, asking them to write their comments on the postcard and send it back to the Fire Department, which will try its best to accept the opinions and improve. In the future, if citizens encounter emergency illnesses, infectious diseases, etc., they can dial 18600, and the ambulance will arrive within five minutes.

Moreover, the "Shanghai Nurses" had just completed the establishment ceremony at 11:00 AM yesterday morning, when the Central Station and the other three stations received a report that Yang Aizhi, a 54-year-old female worker at the Yizhong Tobacco Factory at 733 Changyang Road, had fallen from the escalator and fractured her left tibia and fibula. Nurse Xiao Yongni went with ambulance number 103 and sent her to Hudong Hospital. At 12:17 PM, the Jing'an Temple Station received a report that Wu Lebao, a male resident of 615 Jiangsu Road, was suffering from smallpox. Nurse Wang Linglan went with ambulance number 101 for first aid and sent him to the Municipal First Infectious Disease Hospital. At 1:38 PM in the afternoon, the Central Station received another report that a crazy woman was found at Xuanwu Road, Pingliang Road. Nurse Gu Jian went with ambulance number 103 and sent her to the mental hospital, but she was not admitted. She was then sent to the Red Cross Hospital, but she was not admitted because there were no beds available. The Yangshupu Police Station temporarily took her in.

Citizens' emergency ambulance and nurses. (Photo by China News Agency)

UNRRA's Sixty Fishing Vessels to Be Sold; Method Decided; Price Starts at US$30,000 Per Vessel; Those with Greater Wartime Losses Will Have Priority for Purchase 108

[Our Reporter] The Fisheries Management Office of the Custodial Committee of the Relief and Rehabilitation Commission has previously decided to sell 60 UNRRA fishing vessels to fishermen. The draft detailed sales measures have also been properly formulated by representatives of UNRRA and the Executive Yuan. It was submitted to the Executive Yuan at the beginning of this month, and sales can begin as soon as the Executive Yuan approves it.

According to reporters from relevant parties, the main points of the sales method are as follows: (1) The price of each fishing vessel ranges from US$30,000 to US$120,000, and the legal currency is paid according to the exchange rate of the Central Bank at the time of sale. If the purchaser cannot pay in one lump sum, in order to encourage fishery production, they may be allowed to pay in installments within five years. (2) Any legally registered fishery companies, fishermen, and fishery cooperatives are eligible to apply for purchase. Organizations with better equipment and greater wartime losses will have priority for purchase. (3) Applicants must be carefully reviewed by a committee jointly organized by the Fisheries Management Office, the Fisheries Association, and the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, and only those who pass the examination will be allowed to purchase. It is also learned that to date, the number of applicants to purchase fishing vessels has exceeded 60. All 60 fishing vessels are currently stored at the Fisheries Management Office on Fuxing Island for sale and do not participate in work. Regarding the drivers of new-style fishing vessels, if future purchasers need them, they can also be hired. However, some fishing companies have already sent personnel to the training class there for training and can take up the work immediately after the fishing vessels are purchased.

In addition, the Fisheries Management Office currently has 127 fishing vessels. In addition to the 60 vessels sold and 10% (i.e., 12 vessels) dedicated to training, 50 vessels are retained for fishing and other purposes. However, because these vessels need to be repaired and refurbished successively, only 25 to 30 vessels are frequently used. The Fisheries Management Office plans to establish a company in conjunction with the semi-mechanical wooden boats made by themselves in accordance with the resolution of the Custodial Committee at this conference, and will set up branches in Qingdao, Wenzhou, Yulin, Taiwan and other places, but it is still in the planning stage.

A Glimpse into the Lu Central Campaign 109

[Our Newspaper Jinan 15th Dispatched Telegram] The Communist bandits concentrated the only Ninth Column of the Bi Dong Field Army, and parts of the 13th and 14th Columns (to be verified) from southeastern Shandong and Jiaodong, plus four garrison brigades and four independent regiments, totaling about 50,000 men. Starting at midnight on the 10th of this month, they suddenly launched a pincer offensive towards Zhangdian, Zhoucun, Ganchuan, and Boshan in central Shandong, attempting to repeat their February Laiwu campaign tactics, to encircle and annihilate the National Army's field army. The development of the battle to the present has already proven that history will never repeat itself. Chen Yi's bandit troops' wishful thinking has clearly suffered a severe failure. The Communist bandits launching this pincer offensive were divided into three routes: One route took the Su Town east of Huantai as a base to attack Zhangdian, another took Lucun, the location of the Lu Central Military Region, as a base to attack Boshan, and the third route, which was the main force of the bandits, also took Su Town as a base, divided into groups to cross the Xiaofu River, and scurried to Zhoucun and Huantai.

On the Zhangdian front, the National Army only had one company, and the bandits used more than 4,000 men to encircle and fiercely attack. The National Army, facing a huge disparity in numbers, defended bitterly until noon on the 11th, and finally, due to running out of ammunition and having no reinforcements, the entire company heroically sacrificed themselves. More than 2,000 employees of the Zhangdian Office of the Jiaoji Railway made emergency arrangements when the situation became critical, and retreated westward. However, when they were advancing to the vicinity of Ma Shang Station, they encountered an ambush by the bandit army. Up to now, less than one-fifth have returned to Jinan. What is definitely known is that Engineer Fan Peilun has been captured by the Communist bandits.

The National Army on the Boshan front, due to its weak strength, in order to avoid being "defeated one by one" and "the large eating the small" by the bandits, Wang Yaowu ordered the defending troops, local militias, local Catholic personnel, and miners to all concentrate in Zichuan in an emergency. Zichuan received this support, and its strength doubled. Therefore, from the 11th to the morning of the 14th, Zichuan City and the Fan Hongshan Zibo Coal Mining Company were still in the hands of the National Army. The third route of the Communist bandits was to attack Zhoucun and Huantai, especially Zhoucun, which was their main target of attack. The reason is that this "largest village in the country" is the garrison of Zhou Qingxiang's Reorganized Division of the National Army. The war has been going on since the 11th until the evening of the 12th. In 48 hours, the Communist bandits fired cannons like rain, and launched six frontal assaults, suffering losses of at least more than 5,000 men. In order to achieve his strategic goals and avoid being "eaten," Wang Yaowu used his greatest wisdom to withdraw the entire division to the line north and south of Longshan Station, 33 kilometers east of Jinan City, within 12 hours, to defend the eastern gate of Jinan. Some people believe that the National Army's retreat of more than a hundred miles inevitably caused great suffering to the local people. In fact, if this plan was not adopted, not only might Zhou's troops have been "eaten up," but Jinan would have been even more critical. The reason is that the defense forces of Jinan at that time were unimaginably weak. This preserved the strength, leaving the Communist bandits "empty-handed." At the same time, it also stabilized Jinan City and its surrounding areas.

When the battle of Zhoucun developed to its climax, the Jinpu Railway near Sangnan Station, north of the Yellow River and only ten kilometers away from Jinan City, became tense. General Wang Yaowu used his highest wisdom and greatest perseverance to make the greatest use of this most limited force. The troops on the eastern route quickly relied on the deployment, and part of the troops on the southern route were also concentrated. The originally well-trained militias and volunteer police were fully utilized, making Jinan City a steel city that could not be opened or broken within 24 hours.

Although the collective southward migration of some wealthy merchants and the families of senior and mid-level officers in the pacification area once caused excitement, when they learned that this was Commander Wang's intention to allow his subordinates to have no worries and concentrate on the work of defending Jinan and Shandong, everyone became more calm and stable.

The Possibility of Communist Bandits Invading Jinan is Extremely Low 110

What is currently lingering in the minds of the people of the country is whether the Communist bandits will follow up with a large-scale attack on Jinan? Regarding this question, the reporter's personal answer is that the possibility is very low. The main purposes of the Communist bandits' invasion of Zhoucun, Zhangdian, and other places this time are two: One is to try to use the large to eat the small and eat our Zhou Qingxiang's troops. The second is to try to attract the main force of the National Army to concentrate near Jinan, and then extensively destroy the Pujin section of the Jinpu Railway, especially Xupu, to expand their harassment offensive against northern Jiangsu and northern Anhui, and even threaten the safety of Pukou, so that the representatives attending the National Congress in the capital can hear the sound of artillery and taste a false alarm. If the Communist bandits had the intention of invading Jinan from the beginning, then while attacking Zhoucun and Zhangdian, at least three columns of bandits in southwestern Shandong should have gone north to cut off the central section of the Jinpu transportation in the area north and south of Dawenkou, in order to prevent the northward reinforcements of the National Army from the south. Then, the bandits on the eastern route in Zhoucun would join the bandits to invade Jinan. The Communist bandits did not do this, and they used too few troops this time. Therefore, this can easily help us understand that the Communist bandits have no intention of invading Jinan City on a large scale, at least for the time being.

Reviewing this Shandong campaign, the greatest success of the National Army is that the regular army did not suffer heavy losses. But on the contrary, the local militias rebuilt in Qidong, Huantai, Changshan, Zouping, Zhoucun, and other places failed to fully exert their due power. (Our Newspaper Special Correspondent Li Tian)

Rampaging in Northern Fujian for a Decade, Devouring More Than a Hundred Lives, Giant Tiger from Shunchang Transported to Fuzhou for Exhibition 115

[Our Newspaper Fuzhou 16th Telegram] In the subtropical areas of Guangdong and Guangxi provinces, the breeding of animals and plants is rapid. Carnivorous beasts often easily mingle among them. Fujian Province is especially mountainous, and the mountains are full of wild grass and trees. Over the centuries, stories of wild beasts devouring people and tigers causing trouble have emerged endlessly. Among them, tigers are the most harmful. When people talk about tigers, they all change color. Whenever they hear of "tiger disasters," they often leave their hometowns and take their wives and children far away.

Regarding the distribution of such carnivores in Fujian Province, according to past discoveries and records, they are roughly divided into four categories: The first is the Wuyi Mountain range in northern Fujian, including Jianyang, Shuiji, Chongan, Pucheng, and five or six other counties. On average, there are more than ten tiger disasters every year. The second is the Yong'an, Datian, Youxi, and Shunchang counties in western Fujian, with about a hundred tiger disasters every year. The third is the Jinjiang, Yongchun, Dehua, and Xianyou counties in southern Fujian, with dozens of tiger disasters every year. The fourth is the Ningde, Pingnan, Zhouning, Shouning, and Zhenghe counties in eastern Fujian, with more than ten tiger disasters every year. Among them, the counties in northwestern Fujian are the most common, and the number of people and livestock devoured each year is also greater than in other places. These tigers, small ones "patrol alone," devouring people and livestock that are hidden. Large ones come in groups, knocking on doors and breaking into houses, capturing livestock and children one by one, and then roaring away. The sound of the tiger's roar shakes the mountains and mountains, those who hear it lose their courage, and those who see it are desolate. Therefore, the residents can do nothing about it. Sometimes, in the dark of night, they suddenly hear a tiger's roar, and in the blink of an eye, the tiger arrives, wanting to enter the door. Families often block the door and resist, knocking on utensils to cheer themselves on, hoping that the tiger will be frightened and return to its nest. Over time, people lose all confidence and often regard tigers as divine creatures. Whenever they hear a tiger warning, they burn incense day and night to pray for it to leave. The tragic situation in this is difficult to describe in detail.

The northwestern counties of Fujian Province all have tiger hunting organizations. The method is still to dig traps, install mechanisms, and lure tigers into the shells, then catch and kill them, taking the bones, joints, fat, and blood for medicine, and making tiger skins into clothing. However, in recent years, due to the people's lack of time and the fact that all civilian guns have been confiscated, tiger hunting is no longer possible. Generally new hunters each difficult get involved with mountain area, and launch a surprise attack after waiting. Therefore, in recent years, tiger disasters have tended to intensify. At the opening day of the Fujian Provincial Senate, three or four senators asked the police and security department to train their subordinates to fight tigers and requested that Lu Da add a tiger-fighting course. This humorous conversation was also triggered by this.

The Institute of Zoology and Botany of the Fujian Provincial Research Institute sent Technician Yang Yangyi to Shunchang in the early autumn of last year to collect specimens. Before long, Yang became known for hunting a famous giant tiger in Shunchang. The tiger has now been transported to the Fuzhou West Lake Products Exhibition Hall for public display. The reporter also visited the exhibition a few days ago. The tiger is installed in a glass tree, with a white forehead, hanging eyes, and sharp teeth facing each other. Its body is interspersed with yellow and white stripes, and its ferocious appearance is indescribable. It is about six feet long and more than three feet high, slightly larger than ordinary tigers. According to Wang Yingke, the director of the museum, the tiger has devoured no less than one hundred people in the Shunchang area, and the number of livestock devoured is not included. The eradication of this disaster not only made Shunchang County rejoice, but also made the counties in northern Fujian, which were worried about tiger disasters, happy. It is especially effective in clarifying the erroneous concept of the public "fearing tigers like gods." (Our Newspaper Reporter Huang Zhenqing)

Burma Since Independence - Continued from Page Two 125

Generally speaking, Burma's current political situation seems to be still precarious. The current government claims to be left-leaning and strives to seek welfare for the common people, but its implementation is not thorough and is hampered. As a result, it fails to please both sides. The Communist Party is naturally active in secret, while right-leaning parties representing the interests of the landlord class, led by Ba Maw, the leader of the People's Party, are also eager to rise up. Furthermore, the ruling Socialist Party and the Volunteer Army themselves are not able to cooperate seamlessly. The press corps witnessed several major events during their stay in Rangoon, which offer a glimpse into the situation. One was the arrest of Red Flag Communist leader Thakin Soe in the city on March 12th. Documents seized from him revealed that the Red Flag Party was planning an uprising on March 20th to seize power. Secondly, after the war, Rangoon was filled with street vendors and shacks. The government initially did not interfere in order to please the poor, but later, under the attack and pressure of the landlord class, it ordered the demolition of shacks in a certain area of ​​the city center. This caused protests and petitions from the vendors. The Communist Party took the opportunity to incite them from behind, and the government had to arrest a number of people before the situation was resolved. Thirdly, more than 1,000 workers from the Burma Oil Company went on strike on the 9th, parading in the streets and shouting slogans in a line more than a mile long.

Strike Incident - The labor unrest had not been resolved by the time the press corps left Rangoon. As a result, gasoline was unavailable in Rangoon, and the black market price soared to four rupees per gallon (equivalent to about 400,000 yuan in US dollars), and it was still not easy to buy. The strike was triggered by the dismissal of a worker by a supervisor for spending too long in the toilet. In reality, such a small matter was not enough to justify a major strike, and there was obviously a more complex story behind it.

Destroying Newspaper Offices - Another incident was that on March 12th, members of the Socialist Party held a farmers' and workers' rally at the Shwedagon Pagoda. After the meeting, the crowd destroyed three newspaper offices: the Communist Party's "People's Voice," "Aung Bama," and the right-wing "Economic News." They beat and injured an editor of one of the newspapers and threw a Japanese-style hand grenade, but fortunately it did not explode. The reason for the destruction was that the three newspapers published news insulting Thakin Tin, the Minister of Agriculture and Forestry and one of the leaders of the Socialist Party, accusing him of raping a woman. The content roughly stated that Thakin Tin was on a tour of northern Burma and stayed at someone's house. The daughter of that person was the wife of a driver in the ministry. She had returned home after a quarrel with her husband. Thakin Tin said that he could take her back to Rangoon to reconcile with her husband, but unexpectedly, he raped the woman at a hotel on the way. The news contained obscene descriptions. The day after the news was published, members of the Socialist Party, led by the Secretary of the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, destroyed the three newspaper offices. After the incident, Prime Minister Thakin Nu strongly emphasized the need to maintain law and order in a broadcast and declared that the rioters would be severely punished, but this showed that the upper-level members of the government could not control the lower-level cadres. After this series of events, a "gossip news" item was published in the newspaper on the 14th, stating that the government had issued a curfew and even prohibited groups of more than five people from walking in a row in the busy area near the city hall.

Ethnic Minorities - The issue of ethnic minorities has not been completely resolved in Burma. The ethnic minorities in Burma include the Shans, Kachins, Chins, Karens, and Mons. In order to achieve national unity, the Burmese have tried their best to win over these ethnic minorities. The constitution stipulates that they should be given full autonomy. The current president, Sao Shwe Thaik, is the chief of the Shan people. Although he has no actual power, it can be said that the Burmese have gone to great lengths to please the ethnic minorities. Even so, the Karen people are still demanding autonomy and refusing to participate in the general election. During the press corps's stay in Rangoon, they sent several representatives to Rangoon to negotiate with the government. The outcome is still unpredictable.

Wartime Losses - Burma suffered heavy losses during the war. Destroyed buildings can be seen everywhere in Rangoon. Rangoon University, which occupies 400 acres not far from the city center, has a quiet environment, but its internal facilities can be said to be empty. Most of the school buildings have traces of gray and black smoke on the walls, and the library's collection has been completely burned to ashes. Because it is too poor, it is not known when the post-war reconstruction work can begin. Since independence, the government has formulated a two-year agricultural production increase plan in order to complete the cultivation of 12 million acres of land. Originally, Burma's rice exports before the war reached 3.5 million tons per year, but after the war it was less than 1 million tons. They hope to increase it to 1.5 million tons this year. In addition to increasing production, the government has to greatly increase taxes in order to make up for fiscal revenue. As a result, prices have risen sharply, and the average standard of living has increased by three times compared to before the war. However, the living standards of most Burmese people are extremely low, and Burma is a rice-producing country, so according to their government officials, the lives of ordinary people should not have problems.

Current Cultural Situation - In terms of culture, more than 90% of adults are illiterate. There are more than 20 Burmese and English newspapers in Rangoon, but they are all substandard. The largest newspaper has a circulation of only more than 10,000 copies. Burmese journalists are not as nervous and hurried as those in Shanghai. They have a journalists' association, and most of the news is said to be delivered to their door by government officials. They also have a day off every Sunday, so on Monday, except for a "Monday Express" that is published only on that day, all the others are completely suspended.

In terms of foreign relations, the Burmese can be said to have no strong xenophobia, but because they have just gained independence, just like a young man who has just left the countryside, they inevitably have a naive mentality of pride and arrogance. This is an impression commonly felt by most overseas Chinese in Rangoon. To be honest, the press corps did not have a very good impression of Burma during their ten-day stay in Rangoon. However, this may be because we had too high expectations for this newly liberated country. Therefore, as a brotherly country, we still sincerely wish that this newborn baby can grow stronger day by day and gradually embark on the road to prosperity. (End)

Two Tense Basketball Games: Qingbai Comes from Behind, Renyu Fights Valiantly but Fails, Qingbai Wins by Three Points Against Chenyou, Renyu Loses to Enkas by One Point 151

[Our Report] The 甲 League of the basketball league is nearing its end. The two games last night were unexpectedly tense. Qingbai came from behind to defeat Chenyou by three points with a score of 55-52. In the first half, Chenyou overwhelmed Qingbai with a score of 31-23. In the last minute, Qingbai, in a dangerous situation, won the victory through the efforts of Xu Heng, who can be called the hero of last night. Enkas showed their true colors in the second half to avenge their defeat, resulting in a score of 35-33, only two points ahead. Renyu performed extremely well, but the rainy weather caused few fans to attend.

Qingbai Narrowly Defeats Chenyou

In the first game between Chenyou and Qingbai, the situation within ten minutes seemed to be slightly in favor of Chenyou. Xu Heng scored a free throw, and Qingbai tied the score at twelve points. Afterwards, they competed fiercely, with the score fluctuating. However, Chenyou's style was aggressive. In the first half Chenyou overwhelmed Qingbai with a score of 31-23.

In the second half, Qingbai made personnel adjustments. Zhuo Guorong, Zhang Shaoqing, and Wang Junbing were replaced by Wang Nanzhen, Zhou Dayun, and Chen Xianglong, which showed some improvement. When the opponent added three points, Qingbai suddenly increased by eight points, making the score 34-31. Guorong missed an open shot, Shaoqing made a layup, making the score 35-35. The situation began to change. Aheng made four consecutive free throws, thus catching up with the opponent. Chenyou's Wang Bingfu tied the score at 41-41, and the battle situation fluctuated. In the last three and a half minutes, Qingbai was only leading by two points with a score of 48-46. Chenyou called a timeout. Later, Wang Bingfu became a lucky general, leading 51-50, surpassing Qingbai. Cai Yanxiong committed his fifth foul, Wang made another free throw, Dayun replaced him, Xu Heng's two throws and one penalty made the score 55-52, turning defeat into victory in the last minute.

Enkas Defeats Renyu

In the game between Enkas and Renyu, Renyu first broke the net with a free throw. Enkas scored three points in an instant, but Renyu actually surpassed them again with a score of 7-3. Zhong Yixin's performance was active, and the foreign soldiers were at a loss. This was maintained for fifteen minutes until Ge Pengqi, Gu Gu, and Bao Lai were rampant under the basket, only then did they raise their heads, catching up by one point to 13-12. The momentum changed, and Bao Lai scored another point. In the first half the score was tied at 17. Because both sides were closely marking each other, they both lacked scoring opportunities. In the early part of the second half, Shen Pengju scored a free throw, tying the score at 22. Queli committed a foul, and Shen's two free throws made another contribution, surpassing them by two points. When the score was tied at 24, Zhong committed his fifth foul and was replaced by Li Zhaohe, greatly reducing the team's strength. The foreign soldiers made repeated changes, with Ma Han Fulanke taking turns entering the game, making the score 28-24. Renyu called a timeout, but there was no turnaround. Ma Han scored twice, making the score 32-25. Sun Guozheng was ousted, and Chen Weiyuan replaced him. Wu Xinyun scored in mid-air, and Yao Wenyi scored three points from free throws, closely following behind with a score of 30-32. But time was running out, and Renyu lost to the foreign soldiers by one point with a score of 33-35, Enkas avenging their old hatred.

Page 7

Loan Measures Have Been Concretely Determined: Export Industry is Expected to Improve; Production, Transportation, and Sales Can All Receive Government Assistance 152

The issue of loans for export goods has been thoroughly discussed by all relevant parties and has been concretely determined. It is reported that, in addition to the discounting and packing loans for export goods, which national banks and bureaus will continue to handle as usual, they will also follow the recently approved fixed exchange settlement method for export goods by the Joint Treasury. This method is equivalent to mortgage loans. If an exporter has a transaction with a foreign importer, they can apply for a loan from a national bank or bureau with the order documents. The loan amount is limited to one-tenth of the foreign exchange value of the export goods. For example, if a foreign importer's order is worth US$1,000, the exporter can obtain a loan of US$100 from the national bank or bureau, which will be paid in national currency at the central bank's foreign exchange rate on that day. Exporters who obtain loans must export within a certain period. After the deadline, exporters must sell the export drafts to the lending bank or bureau to repay the loan. This method is more accurate and effective than general mortgage loans. In addition, with the discounting and packing loans, exporters can obtain government funding assistance during the production, transportation, and sales processes. There will definitely be no shortage of funds. Under these circumstances, the export industry is expected to improve in the future. Furthermore, after the implementation of the fixed exchange settlement method, if exporters do not fulfill the exchange settlement conditions, the lending bank or bureau may purchase the collateral.

New Medicine and New Drugs

New Treatment for Post-Illness Limb Paralysis 167

— Liang Junqing

The progress of modern science is gradually tending towards seizing the power of creation and surpassing the ingenuity of nature. Leaving aside the ability of atomic bombs to destroy cities and annihilate the earth, and supersonic aircraft to travel thousands of miles in an instant, the astounding progress in medicine and its tangible benefits to mankind are even more incomparable to atomic bombs and the like. Although the killing power of new weapons such as atomic bombs has shocked the world and left people speechless, their use is limited to one place and one time, which is not as good as medicine that can be used daily to save people and benefit all mankind worldwide. Let me give a few examples to show how great modern medicine is in saving people. For example, diseases like pulmonary tuberculosis, laryngeal tuberculosis, and tuberculous meningitis (commonly known as infantile convulsions) killed countless millions of people in the past, and most doctors have always believed that there was no specific medicine to cure them. However, thanks to the invention of Streptomycin, incurable diseases have become absolutely treatable diseases. Furthermore, diseases such as pneumonia, plague, leukorrhea, syphilis, carbuncles, diabetes, rheumatism, and epidemic meningitis have also claimed the lives of countless millions of people in the past. However, thanks to the increasing progress of modern medicine, these various rare and complicated diseases are no longer a threat to humanity. In addition, conditions such as cerebral hemorrhage (stroke), vascular embolism, and angina pectoris in the elderly, which were previously considered incurable dangerous conditions, are now, although not considered absolutely curable, have their treatment principles fully elucidated, and many people have been cured. As for biological experiments on filterable viruses, cancer treatment, and other research, they are also becoming increasingly sophisticated and approaching the stage of success. From this perspective, the success of medicine in recent years is indeed the greatest among sciences.

Although the progress in medicine has already achieved astonishing results as described above, dedicated medical scientists, biologists, and others are still working tirelessly together, continuously conducting various astonishing and great experimental works in biology. According to recent medical reports, based on years of human biological experiments, it is gradually becoming clear the meaning of human cells in their biological life. In particular, there have been major discoveries regarding the respiration (Zellatmung) of human cell nuclei and cytoplasm. The respiration of the cell nuclei and cytoplasm throughout the human body is significantly related to human physiology, pathology, and the principles of human disease treatment methods. The driving and regulating forces are the three elements of human enzymes (Fermente), hormones (Hormong), and vitamins (Vitamine). According to the inference of the above-mentioned experts, the reasons for human birth, death, illness, and the various responses of external objects to the human body can all be thoroughly understood and used to seek methods of longevity.

Regardless of whether the above theory can become a reality, it has already achieved astonishing success in the research of respiratory enzymes in human cells. According to the report by Dr. Chazitseh of Vienna, Austria, the power of oxidizing enzymes (Oxydase), peroxidizing enzymes (Peroxydase), and catalase (Katalase) can be used to restore the limbs of stroke patients with paralysis and the limbs of children with infantile paralysis to full and normal activity in a very short period of time under certain circumstances. The principles of its treatment are described below:

In the past, doctors believed that the paralysis of limbs caused by diseases, such as the paralysis of infantile paralysis, the paralysis of multiple sclerosis (Multiple Sclerose), the paralysis after stroke, and the paralysis of spinal cord inflammation, were due to the complete destruction of the nerve center, making it impossible to treat. In fact, this is not the case. This dogmatic theory has ceased to exist due to the progress of modern medicine. If the nerve cells and their nerve centers in the patient's body have not been destroyed, they can be restored to their original function by using "enzyme preparations that promote cell respiration."

According to Dr. Chazitseh, there are two types of paralysis after illness: one is the paralysis phenomenon after the nerve cells and nerve centers mentioned above have been destroyed, and the other is the paralysis phenomenon caused by the nerve cells and nerve centers not being damaged, but only the enzyme regulation function having lost its effect. There is currently no method to treat the first type of paralysis mentioned above, while the second type of paralysis can be treated by applying enzyme ointments that "promote cell respiration" to the patient's skin, allowing it to restore its original function in the shortest period of time (often after a few minutes). This is because their nerve cells and nerve centers have not been damaged, but are only in a semi-anesthetized state where they cannot move. After being stimulated by the above-mentioned enzyme preparations, they can restore their mobility in the shortest period of time. This amazing new method of treating paralysis actually originated from the pathological tissue examination of Professor Prof. Marinescu of the University of Hungary, which is that "the respiratory enzymes (Oxydase) of the anterior horn nerve cells of the spinal cord are completely out of balance in those who have suffered from infantile paralysis, causing the limbs to which they belong to become paralyzed." Based on this experiment, Chazitseh continued to study and advocated the use of this enzyme therapy. After years of research by himself and clinical experiments by many scholars, great success has been achieved. Several examples are attached below:

(1) The four-year-old child of an American officer suffered from infantile paralysis two years ago. Afterwards, his left leg was completely paralyzed and he could not move. The muscles of his left hip were also paralyzed and atrophied, which was very obvious. Repeated treatments in the United States for the past two years were ineffective. So he came to Austria for treatment. After being treated with enzyme ointment 20 times, he was able to walk freely and play with other children. He could also go up and down stairs and jump.

(2) A twelve-year-old child suffered from infantile paralysis five years ago. Afterwards, the shoulder muscles were completely paralyzed and he could not raise his arm. After the first treatment with this method, he could raise his arm above his head.

(3) A fifteen-year-old girl suffered from infantile paralysis ten years ago. Afterwards, her legs were disabled and she could not walk at all. Most doctors believed that there was no hope of recovery. A re-examination before the implementation of this therapy also confirmed that her legs were disabled. Unexpectedly, after the first application of the ointment, her disabled right leg could perform knee flexion and extension movements. However, her left leg was still paralyzed as before. But after the second application of the ointment, the left leg could also perform free flexion and extension of the knee. After seventeen applications of the ointment, she was able to stand up and walk.

(4) A worker suffered from multiple sclerosis in 1933. Repeated treatments were ineffective. In 1939, he consulted a professor of neurology in Vienna, but he was considered to have no hope of recovery and was sent to a nursing home. In February 1941, he was treated with this ointment by a doctor and gradually recovered. In August of the same year, he felt energetic and able to return to work, so he requested to leave the hospital and return to work at that time. In September of the same year, he started to work as an assistant to an army doctor.

(5) A gentleman, 52 years old, had suffered from multiple sclerosis for eleven years, which had worsened in the past three years. He usually had to be supported by a nurse when walking. After the first application of this ointment, he saw immediate results and could walk freely without the need for a nurse.

In addition, it has also been proven to have rapid effects on patients with paralysis after stroke, paralysis of myelitis, and severe hearing loss. Due to space limitations, they will not be recorded in detail here. In summary, the invention of enzyme therapy is indeed good news for those suffering from paralysis. If it continues to develop in the future, its prospects will be even greater. Unfortunately, this medicine is a fresh glandular preparation, which must be prepared and used immediately and cannot be stored. We yellow-faced Chinese people are far away and cannot purchase it, so we can only look westward and eagerly await good news. Therefore, the author has already sent a letter to inquire about the manufacturing method, and the details will be revealed later. However, I sincerely hope that the patients in our country will not be disappointed.

History of Inoculation 168

— Hua Xinren

The implementation of immunization methods began with "vaccination against smallpox." In this glorious historical record, we can discover the tortuous progress of "knowledge." At the same time, we should eternally praise the achievements of Edward Jenner, the inventor of this great method. In fact, "inoculation to prevent smallpox" has existed since ancient times. However, using scientific methods like Jenner to inoculate to prevent smallpox is unprecedented in history. We know that smallpox was prevalent in Europe in the 18th century, and people died everywhere. At that time, the only thing that medicine could do to help was to use "pus bubbles from smallpox patients to inject under the skin," which could make smallpox patients less severe. This method was called Inoculation. In Europe, this method was once popular and gained the faith of many people. In 1717, Lady Mary Wortley Montagu, the wife of the British Ambassador to Turkey, wrote a description: "Here, every year in mid-September, some old women specialize in inoculating others against smallpox. At that time, residents often notify each other; those who wish to be inoculated gather in groups of ten or so and ask the old woman to inoculate them. The old woman carries a small box containing smallpox pus. First, she asks the recipient where they want to have their vein punctured. After selecting the spot, she uses a needle to pierce the blood vessel and releases the smallpox pus into the punctured vein... not much pain. Eight days after inoculation, the person experiences alternating chills and fever, and about twenty or thirty smallpox pustules appear on the face. After recovery, no scars remain." Furthermore, according to the records of Dr. Maitland, a physician who strongly advocated inoculation at that time: Princess Caroline of England once asked King George I to pardon six prisoners sentenced to death, as long as they were willing to accept the experiment, they would be released. In 1721, Dr. Maitland boldly conducted this experiment. The results were satisfactory, and the six prisoners were pardoned. In 1774, King Louis XIV of France even accepted this experiment himself and did not experience any adverse reactions. Mademoiselle Rose Bertin, the hat maker for Louis' daughter, Marie Antoinette, even made a women's hat in the form of smallpox pustules to commemorate the King's great contribution. The royal family and nobles enthusiastically accepted the "smallpox inoculation method." Of course, the common people were particularly interested and hopeful, believing that there was a savior for the incurable disease of smallpox. Therefore, they were very enthusiastic about the inoculation method. Among those who excelled in this profession, Thomas Dimsdale was very fortunate at that time because he was not only technically excellent and proficient in dialects but also good at writing. The Russian King heard of his name and specially hired him to go to Moscow to provide guidance. Queen Catherine II first accepted inoculation as a model for the people. At the same time, she ordered her lover, Gregory Orlov, and Duke Paul to be inoculated, and the results were remarkable. From then on, not only must all members of the court follow suit, but even the remote rural areas followed suit in a panic. From these records, we know that the community had already been studying this issue before Jenner invented vaccination. At the same time, the community's awareness of "preventing smallpox" had already been established, but at that time, they only knew that it was so, but did not know why.

Once, it was rumored that the disease from smallpox transmitted from cows was much milder than that transmitted from humans. In particular, milkmaids spoke with certainty about this matter and exaggerated their words. Milkmaids had confirmed that smallpox from cows could be transmitted when milking, due to skin damage and contact with smallpox on the cow's body. Milkmaids were immune to smallpox in an intangible way. A milkmaid once told Jenner that Cowpox could prevent smallpox, and smallpox could not damage her beautiful face. Jenner was very interested and paid close attention to this issue. In 1796, Jenner began his experimental work. He took cowpox pus from the hand of Sarah Nelmes, a milkmaid, and inoculated it into the arm of an eight-year-old child, Philip. Philip became the first hero to contribute to scientific experiments. To commemorate this epoch-making scientific achievement, the famous Italian sculptor Montverde created a bronze statue to praise this eight-year-old child. The infinite horror and psychological fear revealed on the face of this first vaccinated patient tested by Jenner were truly vivid. At that time, Jenner did not have much confidence in doing this experimental work, but other than a pustule on his arm, like the cowpox we see today, Philip did not experience any pain. Three months later, Jenner conducted the second step of the experiment, injecting the poisonous substance from the smallpox pustule under Philip's skin again to test whether the efficacy of the vaccination was reliable. The result confirmed that vaccination could prevent smallpox. Based on these experimental results, Jenner completed a masterpiece in 1798, using a rigorous and upright attitude, insightful and decisive intelligence, and wrote a report entitled "For the investigation of the cause and effect of cowpox as it is called by the people of West England." Not only did it awaken people at that time to pay attention to preventive medicine, but it is also a model for us public health officials to strive for today.

After it spread to the United States, the first person to try Jenner's vaccination against smallpox was Benjamin Waterhouse, a professor at Harvard Medical School. In 1800, he vaccinated his seven children. Moreover, he also made them contact smallpox patients. Unexpectedly, these seven children did not contract smallpox. In 1802, Professor Waterhouse again inoculated nineteen children who had been vaccinated with the dirty smallpox virus under the skin. As a result, two children who had not been vaccinated contracted smallpox, while the other children were safe and sound. After this rigorous experiment, it was further proved that "cowpox is a reliable bodyguard against smallpox" (borrowed from the slogan of the Boston Health Bureau). In 1805, the shrewd and capable General Napoleon ordered the three armies to be vaccinated. This was an indication that the efficiency of promoting the invention of vaccination was faster than any other new medical invention. Unfortunately, due to the slow development of science at that time, the opposition still had great potential. Among them, the people in the church opposed it most fiercely. The excuse for their opposition was that this kind of work violated God's will. The opposition even used the propaganda that people would acquire bovine characteristics after vaccination. But facts speak louder than words, and scientific work won the final victory.

According to the May 1947 issue of Life magazine in the United States: In March, a tourist from Mexico City suddenly died of illness in a hotel in New York City. It was later confirmed to be smallpox. The city's health bureau was shocked upon hearing the report, fearing its spread. Mayor Dewey ordered the city's 175,000 wartime air raid warning agencies to issue alarms. The citizens initially thought a great disaster was coming when they heard the alarm. After the reason was announced, collective vaccination locations were designated, and universal vaccination was implemented. In total, 500,000 people were vaccinated in New York City every day. Within four days, it reached 2 million people. Ten days after this incident, the health authorities were relieved because no new cases were found. If this incident happened in Shanghai, I think the mayor and the director of the health bureau would not have been so "frightened." Because smallpox is a common epidemic in our country.

We must admit that since the invention of vaccination, although smallpox has not yet been eradicated, at the very least, we can say that smallpox is not an incurable disease and can be prevented. Therefore, Jenner's achievements are eternally immortal, just as US President Jefferson said in a letter to Jenner in 1806: "Future generations will know from reading history that the most annoying smallpox since ancient times has been eradicated by you, and now there is no one left." Following this example, up to now, we should make efforts to promote vaccination diligently and seriously. But, even if the words are unobstructed, it is still not without obstacles; otherwise, I will vaccinate myself, and smallpox will still be prevalent, what else is there to say!

Junqing's note: Mr. Hua's article describes the support of Europeans and Americans for vaccination, which is truly inspiring. At present, internal strife is frequent, and smallpox is rampant. Even in Shanghai, smallpox is very rampant. Not only does the authorities not have more complete methods to prevent it, but the general public also has a general attitude of indifference. Alas, "If the people do not fear death, why threaten them with death?" Do the people really not know to fear death? It is only that living is worse than death, so they have no time to fear death. Alas!

Q&A on Medical Affairs from Colleagues 169

— Edited by Liang Junqing

(1) Treatment Methods for Dysmenorrhea

Dr. Zhang asked: There is a 41-year-old woman who has suffered from dysmenorrhea for four years. Every time her period comes, she has back pain, lower abdominal pain, sometimes heavy bleeding, sometimes light bleeding, dark purple color, and lots of leukorrhea. After examination, it was found that there were many cysts on the cervix and mild inflammation, which seemed to be a type of membranous dysmenorrhea. Now, I would like to ask what methods can be used for treatment. Is it possible to use X-rays to destroy the ovaries? Or should a uterine scraping operation be performed?

Dr. Wang replied: The symptoms described in the letter are not very detailed, so I cannot give a definitive answer. However, menorrhagia, dysmenorrhea, and tumors of the uterine adnexa can all occur due to uterine inflammation, and this type of inflammation is mostly tuberculous. According to recent research by many gynecological experts, there are many cases of tuberculosis in the uterus and its adnexa (which is closely related to female infertility), which has not been paid attention to in the past. In addition, the symptoms described in the letter can also occur due to endometritis or perimetritis (which, of course, can also be caused by salpingitis or oophoritis). If you can check the patient's medical history and blood test report (such as the amount of white blood cells, the classification of white blood cells, and the Waaler-Rose test results), as well as the body temperature before and after menstruation, you can determine the nature of the cause of the symptoms. If it is a non-inflammatory uterine adnexal enlargement, it can be removed. The excised material can also be examined histologically. As for the method of uterine scraping, it may not be appropriate, as there may be inflammation present, which may lead to a negative result. Moreover, even if the patient has a state of endometrial tissue hyperplasia and grows in other parts (Endometrio is), uterine scraping will not be effective. Where possible, it is best not to use X-rays to destroy the ovaries, to avoid many negative consequences. However, if there is the aforementioned Endometriosis, then this method can certainly be applied, as this disease is extremely difficult to treat, and even if it is surgically removed, it is not easy to succeed.

(2) Methods to Promote Hair Growth

Dr. Chen asked: Are there any methods to make hair that has fallen out grow back?

Dr. Ma replied: According to recent research results, there is still no reliable and effective hair growth medicine. Twenty years ago, there was a hair growth medicine in Germany called Humagsolan, which was once popular, but then became dormant due to its unreliable effectiveness. Recently, the Swiss Roche pharmaceutical factory has advertised heavily, praising its hair growth medicine "Pintin" as a hair growth vitamin, containing pantothenic acid, namely vitamin B derivatives, which can turn gray hair black, regenerate hair loss, and is based on various chemical tests and clinical reports. Of course, this kind of hair growth element based on vitamins has its theoretical value, but according to personal clinical experiments, its effect is not very obvious. It seems to be far from ideal and still needs to be researched. As for the early stage of baldness, it is hereditary. If it is a general hair loss, it is related to endocrine disorders (namely, the common people call it kidney deficiency), and seborrhea (Seborrhoe) in the scalp is also very relevant. Ultraviolet irradiation of the scalp seems to have a hair growth effect, but its success is very small and it does not last long before the hair falls out again. I think that if the seborrhea of the scalp can be cured, many hair loss situations can be improved except for hereditary ones. As for taking arsenic preparations internally, I have not seen it be effective.

(3) Treatment for Seborrhea of the Face

Dr. He asked: During clinical consultations, young people often come to ask about the cause and treatment of seborrhea of the face. I knew it at the medical school but not in detail, so the treatment was sometimes effective and sometimes not. I wonder if modern medicine has progressed and there are newer theories and treatments?

Dr. Wang replied: Seborrhea of the face is only a local phenomenon. It can also occur in the scalp, ears, neck, and chest. The causes are very complicated. Some are caused by excessive sebum secretion, some are caused by endocrine disorders, some are caused by metabolic disorders in the body, some are caused by abnormal food intake (such as eating too much oily food or eating too much chocolate candy), and some are caused by Flaschenbacillus, etc., all of which are direct or indirect causes. Seborrhea of the face often occurs in conjunction with acne, which must be known. The treatment is best with X-ray irradiation, but it must be performed by an expert and started with the smallest amount. If the dose is too high, it can destroy the main tissues of the skin and cause great harm. Some predecessors used endocrine hormone therapy and saw results. However, the required dose varies from person to person, which is very difficult to measure. Some doctors often fail to obtain the effect due to inaccurate dosage, so they abandon it and do not use it. If the patient has a cause of abnormal food intake, then the treatment must, of course, start from controlling the diet. Sometimes using artificial sun lamps or ultraviolet irradiation is also very effective. As for the local aspect, applying 1-3% salicylic acid preparations or 2% sulfur preparations (such as aqueous solutions, powders, or ointments) may be helpful.

The news of Dr. Fan Shouyuan, a stalwart in our medical community, successfully running for National Assembly delegate has been officially announced in the newspapers in the past few days. This is something we should celebrate. Because Dr. Fan has selflessly dedicated himself to our medical association for the past two years, making his greatest efforts. He has connected the feelings of our medical community, bridged the gaps within our medical community, tried to develop the affairs of the medical association, and strived to eliminate disputes among members. He also used his position as a city councilor to fight for the rights and interests of our doctors in the City Council. How could someone who seeks the welfare of the public without shirking hardship and resentment not be supported by us? Therefore, he received the most votes in this election for representatives to the National Assembly. This is truly what everyone expected. Now that he has been formally elected as a National Assembly delegate, he will certainly continue to use his extraordinary talent in his position as before. This does not need any further addition from us. Well done, Dr. Fan! We celebrate your success, which is also the success of our medical community.

Random Thoughts 171

— Pingzhai

Before the war, a ten-dollar bill could buy a picul of rice. Now, no one would even pick it up if it were dropped on the ground. If you used a ten-dollar bill to light a cigarette, it would probably be cheaper than using a match.

A few days ago, when I hailed a rickshaw, I saw a thousand-dollar bill on the seat cushion. I told the rickshaw puller that there was money on the seat. Four or five rickshaw pullers standing nearby all gathered around to look. When they saw it was only a thousand dollars, they all burst into laughter. In the end, the rickshaw puller I hailed stuffed it into his pocket, but I heard his companions making fun of him: "What a disgrace!" "What a big appetite!"

It seems that picking up a thousand-dollar bill is already an "embarrassing" thing.

At the same time, everyone taking the tram feels the trouble of making change, especially now that there is a one-level fare of six thousand yuan. Both passengers and ticket sellers feel a headache. It is certainly not acceptable for passengers to pay five thousand yuan, as that would be "cheating," and the ticket seller would definitely not be polite. But if you pay ten thousand yuan and ask for change, the ticket seller often does not have that many one-thousand-yuan bills. As a result, most people naturally accept the ten thousand yuan, give you a six-thousand-yuan ticket, and say "Thank you!" Many passengers do not care about the four thousand yuan change anyway, and gradually become accustomed to it.

However, some passengers feel that they have been taken advantage of, or that regardless of how small the matter is, it violates the principle of integrity, and they inevitably argue. This usually begins with the passenger's face turning red and ends with the ticket seller's sarcastic remarks.

Thus, every Shanghainese feels a kind of contradiction: when going to the bank to withdraw money, they fear that the bank will give them "bad bills." If you want to withdraw ten million, and they give you bills with a face value of only five thousand yuan, you may already feel impatient. If they give you bills of one thousand yuan or even five hundred yuan, then no matter how good your usual self-cultivation is, you cannot help but lose your temper and say that the bank clerk is deliberately working against you. When receiving money, for the sake of convenience, the face value of the bills is feared to be too small, and the bills are feared not to be new enough. But on the tram, you fear that your pockets are full of brand-new five-thousand-yuan Customs Gold Unit bills, because making change takes time, and sometimes it will cause you to miss your stop.

I have a classmate named Li, who studies literature and has a particularly rich imagination. He often likes to fantasize about the history of those tattered banknotes. He often says: "Maybe this bill was once held by a beggar covered in sores; maybe it has been in the hands of someone with leprosy... How terrible, how terrible!" So he always keeps an empty glass bottle containing aspirin pills with him, and the surface of his clothes is full of alcohol. Whenever he inevitably receives a slightly worn banknote, he always pours a little alcohol into his palm and quickly rubs the fingers that touched the banknote in the alcohol, saying it is "disinfecting." However, he always carries some of those small bills that he considers terrible, because he hates wasting time. Whether buying things or buying tram tickets, whenever there is a fraction, he must make it up to the exact amount, and then happily leave.

In fact, customers like Mr. Li are certainly welcomed by all stores or honest ticket sellers, because they are straightforward and the transaction is done smoothly. However, there are probably not many people like Mr. Li in the world, especially in Shanghai, there is probably only him alone. Thus, the problem of making change, a problem for most Shanghainese today, remains unresolved.

But the headache of the change problem is not unique to China. Foreign countries also have it, and this "foreign country" is actually the most opulent America.

In the few years after 1860, America experienced a major shortage of change. Various companies and businesses automatically manufactured some "token coins" (which were coins, not the "token vouchers" that appeared in wartime Shanghai). The company's brand name and address were printed on the token coins, and the other side was printed with words such as "a loaf of bread" or "a bottle of beer." More than ten thousand stores used these "token coins," and at least twenty-five million "token coins" were in circulation. But in 1864, the owner of a bar in New York actually refused to redeem them after issuing twenty thousand beer token coins! As a result, the owner was of course arrested, and the American government also promulgated a law prohibiting private minting of any currency. "Token coins" then disappeared and became a historical term.

But what really solved America's change shortage was not any legal force, but the American government's complete overhaul of the issuance amount of coins. When there are more "dimes," making change is no longer a problem.

Perhaps it is still too early to talk about reforming the currency system today, but if we are not reforming, then when we do reform, we should really let our pockets often hear the clinking sound of "dimes" colliding.

The Greatness of the World 172

— Le

The largest fish caught by a fisherman with a fishing rod was a great white shark caught by Australian Cal Howell on May 12, 1941. This shark was fourteen feet eight inches long, with a girth of eight feet and a half inch, and weighed one thousand nine hundred and nineteen pounds.

The strangest record in the United States was recorded by a black jazz musician named Pechitol, who played six different instruments at the same time: one soprano saxophone, one baritone saxophone, one trumpet, one piano, one cello, and drums. During the recording, the music for the first instrument was recorded first, and after it was finished, the music for the second instrument was recorded on the same record, continuing six times in a row. The name of this piece of music is "Priest."

When Westerners drink different kinds of wine, connoisseurs use different wine glasses. Therefore, first-class restaurants and hotels must have at least sixty sets of wine glasses of different shapes and sizes.

Although the facilities in American prisons are good, prison breaks still occur frequently. Previously, prison guards were often not punished when prisoners escaped. Recently, the United States Congress passed a law that when a prison break occurs, the prison guard should be convicted of dereliction of duty, fined five hundred US dollars, and sentenced to one year in prison.

Old Stories of Peking University 173

— Jiefu

I recently read an article in the "Free Discussion" section of the Shen Bao written by Ling Xiaohange, "Friends of My School," discussing the past of Peking University. It is truly comforting to learn some details from this, as I have not heard from old friends for decades. I was in the same class as Ling Xiaohange. I have been working in the engineering field and sometimes feel happy enough to pick up a pen and publish articles. My old friend probably still remembers the name "Jiefu" from the early Republic of China. When we talk about the past of "Peking University" today, it is like a white-haired palace woman of the Tang Dynasty talking about the relics of the Tianbao era. Ling Xiaohange's account still has omissions, so I will add one to respond and inform the alumni of Peking University.

When the Qing Dynasty first established Peking University, it set up four departments: Shixueguan (Literary Study Hall), Jinshiguan (Scholars' Hall), Shifanguan (Teachers' Hall), and Yixueguan (Translation Hall). The first two halls were set up for those who passed the imperial examinations to make up for their lack of modern learning. Mr. Ye Yu-fu (Gongchuo) was a student of Shixueguan, and Mr. Guan Ying-ren (Genglin) was a student of Jinshiguan. Shifanguan was set up to prepare teachers for establishing schools, and Yixueguan was to cultivate talents for translating Western books. Yixueguan had many handsome young men, and was known as the "Xianggong Tangzi" (Elegant Gentlemen's Hall) at the time. Wu Jinglian, the speaker of the first National Assembly of our country, and Zhu Zhaoxin, the former special envoy of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Guangdong and Guangxi, were both students of Shifanguan. Mr. Gu Mengyu was a student of Yixueguan. There were many others who held important positions or were well-known at the time. These are just a few examples casually mentioned. Later, in preparation for establishing a university with specialized departments, a university preparatory course was first set up, and students were recruited from various provinces and sent to Beijing to study. I was one of the twenty-four preparatory students from Guangdong Province at that time. At that time, there were very few talents in modern learning in the country, so most of the professors in other subjects besides Chinese Studies were foreign, from England, America, Germany, France, Russia, Belgium, Japan, and the Netherlands. It could almost be called an international school.

The head of the university was not initially called the president, but the "University Superintendent," with the rank of a third-grade Beijing official concurrently serving in the position. The position was quite high, and those who held this position were all well-known figures. I remember that Mr. Yan Jidao (Fu) once held this position. Yan had a foot ailment. Every time he arrived at the school, he got out of the car at the gate and then rode in a two-person sedan chair to the superintendent's office. He also smoked opium. The students criticized him for being old and corrupt, and created a cartoon of someone smoking opium, published in the newspaper, titled "Smoke Recovery." Yan was embarrassed and soon resigned. He was succeeded by Mr. Ma Xiangbo (Liang), who was nearly eighty years old at the time. The students thought he was too old, and sent several representatives to see him, telling him: "Peking University is not easy to run. Mr. Yan has already retreated because he found it difficult. You are so old, why bother looking for trouble? Wouldn't it be better to rest at home? If it's for the monthly salary of three hundred yuan, that's easy to solve. We students can pool three hundred yuan a month and send it to you!" Old Mr. Ma laughed and said repeatedly: "Bring it to me! Bring it to me!" Ma was quite humorous and eloquent. The next day, he summoned the students for a speech, saying: "What is called a university is not because the school's buildings are big, the students' tempers are big, or the principal's age is big (what else is big, I don't remember clearly), but it is because of how it should be to be worthy of being called a university," and so on. But Mr. Ma did not stay in his position for long, resigning after a few months, which shows that the sharpness of Peking University students did not begin with the May Fourth Movement.

Lincoln Polishing His Shoes 174

— Gonghua

One morning in the White House.

Secretary of State Jim was led by a messenger to a large living room to see President Lincoln on official business. As he walked down the corridor, he saw a man beside him who was constantly polishing his shoes. Jim inadvertently looked down and stopped in surprise.

President Lincoln was constantly polishing his own shoes.

"Your Excellency, as President, doing such a thing is not very elegant when seen by others, especially by noble ladies..." Secretary Jim usually heard people say behind his back that the President often showed crude manners like a country bumpkin, and he blurted it out today.

Then Lincoln smiled and looked at Jim's surprised eyes; "Ah! Is polishing shoes a shameful thing? Mr. Jim! That is not right. The President and the shoe polisher are both public servants working for the world. There should be no lowly occupations in the world, only people with base hearts."

Lincoln said loudly, and with hands still stained with shoe polish and other smells, he took the important official documents brought by Jim and began to read them with the same enthusiasm as when he was polishing his shoes.

Anecdotes of Einstein 175

— Leng Leng

The father of the theory of relativity, Einstein, was slow, shy, and spoke incoherently as a child. His parents worried that his talent was not as good as ordinary children, and the teachers in school shook their heads in despair, calling him a dunce and thinking that he was hopeless and uneducable. Who knew that such an incredibly clumsy child would be recognized as one of the most outstanding intelligent giants of our time, one of the greatest thinkers of ancient and modern times, sixty years later?

Einstein regarded fame, wealth, and luxury with extraordinary indifference; it is said that once, the captain of a ship on the Atlantic Ocean, in order to treat Einstein well, specially gave up the most exquisite room on the ship to wait for him, but he was severely rejected, unwilling to accept this special treatment, and preferred to sleep in the lowest-class steerage. When he was hired by Princeton University in New York, USA, to go to lecture, in order to avoid the trouble of interviews with reporters, he instructed his friends in advance to secretly pick him up by barge halfway before the ship arrived at the port and transfer him to a car to drive to the school.

Currently, at least nine hundred books have been published explaining Einstein's theory of relativity, but according to Einstein himself, only twelve people in the world can truly understand his theory of relativity, and his wife is also an exception.

Einstein once used a simple example to explain relativity; a beautiful girl sits with you for an hour, and you feel like it is only a minute; if you sit alone by the stove for a minute, you feel like it is an hour. - At first, it seems to make some sense, but it is actually relativity.

According to Einstein's wife: her husband is very willing to abide by order in his thoughts, but in real life, he is willing to adopt casualism, unwilling to be bound by order, and wants to do whatever he wants to do whenever he wants to do it. He has set two rules for himself; one is that no matter what "rules" are, he does not want them, and the other is that he is not controlled by anyone's opinions.

But sometimes he has to violate the second rule when he meets his wife; for example, when she invites friends to a tea party at home, she wants to ask her husband to participate in their grand meeting, but Einstein often answers harshly: "No! No! I can't go! I can't go! I can't stand such harassment, which makes me unable to work in peace, I want to leave this place immediately!"

Einstein's wife is really patient, waiting for him to finish his anger, and then uses a few good words to make him obediently follow her downstairs to participate in their tea party.

Einstein's daily life is very simple. He usually wears a set of untidy old clothes, does not like to wear a hat often, and often whistles or hums songs in the bathroom. Although he intends to solve the complicated mysteries of the universe, he believes that he cannot make the enjoyment of life too complicated, so when he shaves after bathing, he does not use shaving soap but uses bath soap, because he thinks two kinds of soap is really a waste.

There are really many anecdotes about Einstein, let me tell one more to end it! One day, he argued with a ticket seller on a bus in Berlin, because he thought the change was wrong. After the ticket seller recounted the change, he realized that Einstein himself was wrong, so he returned the change to him and said a humorous sentence that was almost mocking our great mathematician and thinker: "This time the mistake is because the gentleman cannot count!"
