Poetry Record of the Sea Red Mansion 177

— Xu Banmeng

Sending to a Friend

After parting, the border river is urged by horns, the frost wind is bleak and tight on the night of the stage, the three lives of the mind are thousands of folds of clouds, ten thousand miles of home mountains are a cup of wine. Laughing at the fish and dragons working on acrobatics, leisurely inviting apes and cranes out of the dust, old friends are scattered and few confidants, and the flames of war are everywhere.

Receiving a Friend's Letter and Sending Back

Where do you want to go in all directions, how long will you invite me to drink painfully, heroes on the sea leave the ramparts, elders in Jiangdong look forward to banners; rivers and mountains return me to the divine state, singing and crying follow people, the country's destiny moves, how many new tears of Bao Xu, where to find the bells and instruments in the southern accent!

Drunk

Who lined up the sky howling on the high platform, ten thousand miles of clouds and rainbows are extremely sad, a good head is thrown in one lonely bet, the ruthless universe is old and ash! Hardship is the blessing of mediocrity, destruction is also the talent of construction, alas, my life is over, I lie drunk in the Artemisia.

Intending to Return, Composed Orally

The river flows east, the sea sun sets west, the scenery of Jingnan is unbearable, the dream of returning home is gradually distant and faint, listening to the cuckoos crying year after year.

The Collector's Seal 178

—

"Collecting" is considered the most sympathetic of all hobbies. Books, paintings, card versions, bronzes, porcelains, everything enriches knowledge, broadens horizons, and nourishes the spirit, which is more brilliant than wild dancing, gambling, and the plays of eroticism, pornography, blacklists and whitelists. However, it also requires a kind of wisdom to control and balance it. If you are too obsessed or enter the realm of madness, it will not be beneficial, but will be a burden, unable to broaden your mind, but instead blocking your intelligence.

In the early years of the Daoguang period of the Qing Dynasty, Hanlin Sun (Yuanxiang) of Changshu wrote a preface to Qian Meixi of Jinkui's "Shu Tan," saying about "collecting": "It is generally like clouds and smoke passing by. Qian himself also said in a book: 'Collecting is an elegant matter, originally like clouds and smoke passing by, which can pass without staying. If you are greedy and covetous, it will turn elegance into vulgarity. Look at the collectors of ancient times, none of them have passed it down to their descendants for hundreds of years who can still keep it!'" The words are extremely insightful.

The words "collecting" and "passing by" seem contradictory on the surface. Since it is regarded as smoke and clouds passing by, why bother to collect it tightly? Therefore, Qian said: "Gao Jiangcun already said that people exhaust their resources to engage in collecting, which is no different from risking their lives to seek wealth and glory. And there is also a small seal that says: 'Jiangcun's thirty years of effort gathered.' It can be seen that he loves it deeply and is deeply addicted to it, and may not be able to regard it as clouds and smoke passing by." In fact, hobby is a mood, and collecting is a natural fact, which is not contradictory to "optimism." Mr. Qian himself was a great collector, and at the same time an optimist.

Yuan Hanyun of Xiangcheng was an accomplished man of literature and art, and loved antiquity as if it were his life. He had a large and exquisite collection of items, and his versions were much richer than those of his friends. He once engraved a seal with the inscription "May descendants always treasure it." Later, he felt that his hopes were too extravagant, and changed the seal to "Exist and perish with the body." It can be said that he was extremely saddened, but it was only a temporary emotional effect. Later, he lived in extreme poverty in Tianjin, and he could not avoid selling his beloved items for money. Then the descendants would certainly not always treasure them, and the individual would sometimes find it difficult to coexist with them. Therefore, what his seal expressed was only his own deep infatuation at the time.

Hanlin Ye Juchang of Suzhou spent his life searching for rubbings of steles and various rubbings. His Ruyuan Diary was never without some "post sellers" and "stele appraisers." In the year of Bing Shen, his only son died of illness, and he was endlessly saddened, saying that "the family heir has died, and the pillars of the hall have no one to rely on," and also saying that "the old paper in the box, I don't know whose hands it will fall into in the future!" He also said: "Who will collect and organize my life's painstaking searches in the future? Speaking of it makes me even more sad!" It seems that old Mr. Ye also hoped that "descendants would always treasure it." If a person has no descendants, the legacy will eventually be scattered. Two years later, the son of the deceased Hanlin Huang sold his father's treasures to Liulichang. Old Mr. Ye sighed and wrote down a few words: "Huang Benfu came to talk, and reunited the legacy with 2,800 gold to return it to the factory. If a son can read, he still cannot keep it. We can see through the illusion!" So he suddenly realized.

It turns out that the saying of preserving for generations originated in feudalism and was advocated by emperors. The imperial jade seal in history, as well as the words "eternal treasure" engraved on palace tripods and bells, can all prove the same meaning as the so-called "passing it down to all ages" and "the country's destiny is boundless."

Collectors often prepare some seals with the inscriptions "family collection," "family inheritance," etc., and stamp them on the steles, paintings, and books they collect. As a result, as Qian said and Ye lamented, they will inevitably be scattered elsewhere. Because there are no descendants, or the descendants are unworthy, or there are sons who can read but are intolerably poor, or the times are chaotic, or the cities change, all can break the reality of "family inheritance." Not to mention antiques, even houses, fields, and large mansions change owners and surnames. The emperors always say that they will be boundless for generations, but it is just a good-sounding word, a good-looking pattern. Not only is it impossible in fact, but it is also unnecessary in principle. Good things can be appreciated by everyone. If they are permanently locked in one family and one surname, it is not truly cherishing antiques.

The seals of gentlemen with clearer insights are not like that. They choose the words "Succession and Guarding" to verify that a certain object once belonged to the descendants of a certain predecessor, and they are considered a guardian who "continues to guard" it, and hint that if it is transferred to someone else's hands in the future, they also hope that he can recognize the goods and preserve them, such as Hanlin Li Lianxiu's rubbings, which are stamped with "Lianxiu Succession and Guarding," which is to cherish precious objects, not selfishness, is the succession of responsibility, not the succession of family, is "passing on to the worthy" rather than "passing on to the son," which has the atmosphere of "the world is for all" and the spirit of thoroughly cherishing things. Furthermore, "Once collected in a certain place," and the certain place is the name of the current owner. The prefix "Once" means that sooner or later it will belong to others, and "Once in my hands" is also optimistic. When others get it in the future, they will definitely laugh when they see the seal. He has already said it in advance.

Because of this, in many rubbings, both before and after, and even in the heaven and earth margins, various kinds of inscriptions such as "Someone's collection," "Someone's guarding," "Someone's seen," "Someone's," and "Someone's family" are stamped, which is very lively, and people who buy rubbings are even more interested in this, because it has been proven by many predecessors. At the same time, these seals have become treasures to be researched and appreciated, and the interest in them is perhaps even stronger than the original rubbings.

Qian Meixi also said that collectors are divided into three classes: one is appreciation, the second is good deeds, and the third is profit. Those who seek profit imitate hundreds of times and forge thousands of times to obtain money and goods, which are petty people in the market. According to this, it is the so-called "antique ghost." Imitation, interception, fumigation, its techniques are diverse, but no matter what, it cannot escape the eyes of true appraisers. The first method for identifying the authenticity of old and new is to focus on "charm" and "spirit." Those who "make old" can never compare to "true old," and those who imitate can never mix with genuine products. At the Pingdian Fair in Beiping, imitations of celebrity ink paintings from the Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties are available, and the paper, silk, and brushwork are also very good, but the imitation products must have several flaws. If you don't see it at first glance, you will understand it after another look.

In recent years, the cost of living has risen, and old families have released many fine products. Banmeng's letter stated that there are real prices and real things in Shanghai. The first page of a Yuan and Ming manuscript is Song Xue's original ink painting, and someone bought it for 400 million, which is not too expensive (converted to current foreign currency, it is limited)! Liu here has more than a dozen volumes of Song Xue's figure paintings, each with Song Xue's own inscription. Shao Yu's nephew introduced me to see them and asked me to appraise them. After viewing them, the spirit and energy were gathered, and there was no doubt that they were genuine works. An antique dealer has offered ten yellow goods, but the original owner is still unwilling to sell them, which shows how much he cherishes them.

Carefree Flowers 179

— Chen Shenyan

Chapter Twelve: A Chance Encounter (102)

That evening, Qi Wan returned to the Middle East Hotel. Dao Yun had already returned. Qi Wan didn't reveal a single expression. Upon seeing him, she smiled and said, "You're busy with work. I couldn't wait for you, so I went to see my mother today. My mother was very happy to see me in Shanghai, and she strongly approves of our matter. She only blamed me for not going with you today. I promised her that I would definitely pay my respects tomorrow, no matter what. You must set aside any important matters you have tomorrow and take care of this first. Otherwise, the old lady will be angry!" Dao Yun was very worried when he first heard that Qi Wan had gone to see her mother, but when he heard that Liu Ru had no objections to Qi Wan's marriage, he felt relieved and said, "Of course we must go. I originally planned to prepare everything for us before paying my respects to my future mother-in-law. Now that you've told her, then my planned schedule will have to change. I'll go with you first thing tomorrow morning." Qi Wan said, "That's not necessary. My mother doesn't get up until two o'clock every afternoon!" Dao Yun said, "Then we'll wait until after two o'clock to pay our respects. What gifts should we bring?" Qi Wan said, "You decide that. I won't offer any suggestions." Dao Yun said, "We came in such a hurry that we didn't bring any Beijing specialties. I can't think of what gifts to prepare now." Qi Wan said, "Why bother racking your brains over these things? My mother doesn't care about this. As long as you can please her when you meet her, that's the best thing." Dao Yun said, "I'm sure I can please her. She already likes me. Now that we're becoming relatives, and you're her most beloved daughter, there's no reason why she wouldn't like me." Qi Wan said, "I hope so!" Dao Yun didn't know what Qi Wan meant when she said that, so he didn't dare to ask any further questions. That night passed. The next morning, Dao Yun was busy going out to prepare gifts. At two o'clock in the afternoon, the two of them took a car to Mingde Lane to pay their respects to Liu Ru. When Liu Ru saw Dao Yun, she showed great affection, asking about his well-being and saying that she was very pleased to have this marriage connection. Afterwards, she asked him about his plans for the film production company. Dao Yun knew that Liu Ru had a lot of connections in the Shanghai film circle and that her information was very accurate, so he claimed that the headquarters were in Hong Kong. Although he reluctantly pointed out that many financial backers were helping, his words were not very natural. Liu Ru, who was experienced in worldly affairs, saw through Dao Yun's unreliable words after only a few questions. Immediately, she didn't reveal her true feelings and indulged him with flattery. She kept them for dinner before sending him back. When he was leaving, she secretly instructed Qi Wan to come again tomorrow. Qi Wan, after receiving this signal from Liu Ru, became even more disgusted with Dao Yun.

Seeking Talents 180

(1) A certain dental clinic in this city is seeking a male dental assistant. (2) A certain unit outside the city is seeking a male music instructor. (3) A certain unit is seeking a male art instructor (high school level or above). (4) A certain agency in this city is seeking a male librarian (specialized library management graduate). (5) A certain cigarette paper shop and a certain thread factory in this city are seeking apprentices. (6) A certain radio company in this city is seeking a male decorating technician. (7) A certain foreign dentist in Taishi is seeking a female (fluent in English) dental assistant. (8) A certain school for the deaf and dumb outside the city is seeking a female teacher and accountant. Those who wish to apply for the above positions, please come in person to the Shanghai Employment Agency of the Ministry of Social Affairs, No. 856 North Sichuan Road in this city for an interview (due to time constraints, only residents of this city are eligible).

[Another News] A certain agency outside the city is seeking the following talents, with excellent compensation. Those who wish to apply, please send a letter to Mr. Wu Yixin, 3rd Floor, No. 89 Danmen Road, Shanghai. If suitable, you will be contacted for an interview. No replies will be given if not suitable.

In addition to writing a "Biography," the director must write "My Views on Actor Selection and Training," and the playwright must write propaganda scripts for "Conscription" and "Road Construction," and attach a resume.

Shanghai Tuberculosis Sanatorium Offers Preferential Treatment to Public School Teachers 181

The Shanghai Tuberculosis Sanatorium, considering that public school teachers have heavy workloads and difficult lives, and if they are troubled by illness and medical expenses, it is unbearable. In order to help public school teachers reduce their burden, the sanatorium has specially stipulated that every Sunday morning from 9:00 to 11:00, during off-duty hours, the cost of taking a chest X-ray photo will be reduced by half, temporarily charging 500,000 yuan. Artificial pneumothorax surgery will be performed, and patients will stay in ordinary wards. The surgical fee will be waived during the hospitalization period as preferential treatment.

This Newspaper's Wuzhou, Guangxi Reader Enquires About a Correspondence School for Poultry Farming 182

Respected Editor: I am a reader of your newspaper. Before the war, in 1939, I was introduced by your newspaper to the Deyuan Poultry Correspondence School in Shanghai, where I studied the complete course of chicken farming with Mr. Huang Zhongcheng. Since the enemy occupied Guangzhou and then invaded Wuzhou, I have lost seven-tenths of the complete set of books, which I find very regrettable. Now I would like to trouble the editor to inquire whether the Deyuan Poultry Correspondence School, which existed in Shanghai before the Japanese occupied Shanghai, still exists? What is the current address? And the address of Mr. Huang Zhongcheng, and where in Shanghai can his complete chicken farming book still be purchased? I respectfully request a reply! Sincerely, Reader Peng Runbiao, Correspondence Address: Wanxingxiang, Xiaonan Road, Wuzhou, Guangxi.

Mao Tianzhi 1,000,000 yuan, Ru Xiting 400,000 yuan, Shi Wenlin 100,000 yuan. The total amount received above is 1,500,000 yuan, bringing the total to 236,804,290 yuan.

Furthermore, from now on, if there are such donations, please send them directly to the association's collection banks. This newspaper will no longer collect them on its behalf. This is a special announcement.
